  B: (85,9)
  C: (50,7)
  D: (1,1)
  E: (1,0)

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 2 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If 75 percent of the employees of a certain company take a winter vacation, 40 percent take a winter and a summer vacation, and 20 percent take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, what Q percent of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation?
Choices:
  A: 5%
  B: 15%
  C: 25%
  D: 35%
  E: 45%
Response 0:
Knowledge:
Let's assume that the total number of employees in the company is 100.
If 75% of the employees take a winter vacation, then 25% of the employees do not take a winter vacation.
If 40% of the employees take both winter and summer vacations, then 35% of the employees take only summer vacation.
If 20% of the employees take neither winter nor summer vacations, then 80% of the employees take at least one of these vacations.

Q percent of employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation = (Percentage of employees who take only summer vacation) - (Percentage of employees who take both winter and summer vacation)

Action: 
Percentage of employees who take only summer vacation = 35%
Percentage of employees who take both winter and summer vacation = 40%
Therefore, Q percent of employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation = 35% - 40% = -5%

Since the answer is negative, it means that none of the choices is correct. Hence, we can conclude that "None of the Above" is the most likely answer.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the total number of employees in the company is 100.
  75 percent of the employees take a winter vacation, which is 75 out of 100.
  40 percent take a winter and a summer vacation, which is 40 out of 100.
  20 percent take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, which is 20 out of 100.
  We need to find the percentage of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
  Let's assume that Q percent of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.
  Therefore, the number of employees who take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation is (Q - 40) percent.
  The number of employees who take either a winter or a summer vacation is (75 + Q - 40) percent.
  The number of employees who take no vacation is 20 percent.
  Therefore, (75 + Q - 40) + (Q - 40) + 20 = 100.
  Solving the equation gives Q = 45.

Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  The formula for calculating percentages in a Venn diagram is: 
  Q = 100% - (A + B - AB) - Neither
  where A is the percentage of people in the first category, B is the percentage of people in the second category, AB is the percentage of people in the intersection of the two categories, and Neither is the percentage of people in neither category.
  
  We know that 75% of employees take a winter vacation, which means 25% do not take a winter vacation. We also know that 40% of employees take both winter and summer vacations, meaning that 35% take only a winter vacation. Finally, we know that 20% of employees take neither vacation, leaving 80% who take at least one vacation.

Action: 
  Q = 100% - (75% + 35% - 40%) - 20%
  Q = 100% - 70%
  Q = 30%
  
Answer:("30%")
Response 3:
Let's assume that there are 100 employees in total. Then, we can calculate the number of employees that take a winter vacation, a summer vacation, both, or neither as follows:

- 75 employees take a winter vacation (75% of 100).
- 40 employees take both a winter and a summer vacation (40% of 100).
- 20 employees take neither a winter nor a summer vacation (20% of 100).

To find the number of employees that take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation, we can use the formula:

(number of employees that take a summer vacation) - (number of employees that take both a winter and a summer vacation)

We already know that 40 employees take both a winter and a summer vacation. To find the number of employees that take a summer vacation, we can use the fact that 20% take neither a winter nor a summer vacation, which means that 80% take at least one vacation. Therefore, the number of employees that take a summer vacation is:

0.8 * 100 = 80 employees

So, the number of employees that take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation is:

80 - 40 = 40 employees

To find the percentage of employees that take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation, we can divide this number by the total number of employees (100) and multiply by 100:

40/100 * 100 = 40%

Therefore, the answer is 40%, which corresponds to choice E.

S% = 100% - 35% - 40% - 20%
 
S% = 5%

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 3 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A rectangular solid, 3 x 4 x 15, is inscribed in a sphere, so that all eight of its vertices are on the sphere. What is the diameter of the sphere?
Choices:
  A:  13.3542
  B:  15.8113
  C:  18.3451
  D:  19.5667
  E:  20.8888
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The diameter of a sphere is twice the length of its radius.
  The space diagonal of the rectangular solid is equal to the diameter of the sphere.
  The space diagonal of a rectangular solid with dimensions a, b, c is equal to sqrt(a^2 + b^2 + c^2).

Action: 
  The space diagonal of the rectangular solid is sqrt(3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2) = sqrt(250).
  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the space diagonal of the rectangular solid, which is sqrt(250).
  We can simplify this to 5 * sqrt(10).
  Therefore, the answer is 2 * 5 * sqrt(10) = 10 * sqrt(10).
  Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The diameter of a sphere is twice the length of its radius.
  The length of the space diagonal of a rectangular solid can be found using the Pythagorean theorem.
  The space diagonal of the rectangular solid is the diameter of the sphere.
  The Pythagorean theorem states that the square of the hypotenuse of a right triangle is equal to the sum of the squares of the other two sides.

Action: 
  The space diagonal of the rectangular solid can be found using the Pythagorean theorem:
  d^2 = l^2 + w^2 + h^2
  d^2 = 3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2
  d^2 = 9 + 16 + 225
  d^2 = 250
  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the space diagonal of the rectangular solid:
  diameter = d
  diameter = sqrt(250)
  diameter = 5 * sqrt(10)
  Therefore, the answer is approximately 15.8113.
  Answer: ("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  A rectangular solid can be inscribed in a sphere if the diameter of the sphere is equal to the space diagonal of the solid.

  Given a rectangular solid with sides a, b, and c, the space diagonal can be calculated as sqrt(a^2 + b^2 + c^2).
  In this case, a = 3, b = 4, and c = 15.

  Calculate the space diagonal of the rectangular solid:
  space_diagonal = sqrt(3^2 + 4^2 + 15^2) = sqrt(250) = 5sqrt(10)

  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the space diagonal of the solid:
  diameter = 2 * space_diagonal = 10sqrt(10)

  Round the diameter to two decimal places:
  Action: Answer("A")  (13.35 is the closest option)

  Given the dimensions of the rectangular solid, l = 3, w = 4, and h = 15.

  The diameter of the sphere is the hypotenuse of a right triangle with legs equal to the diagonal of the rectangular solid.

  Therefore, the diameter of the sphere is 32/2 = 16.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 4 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Peter wants to find 10 additional people to form a scavenger hunt team with him. If he has 10 friends who would like to participate, how many choices does he have for forming his team?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 1
  C: 2
  D: 3
  E: 4
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Peter has 10 friends to choose from to form his team.
  He needs to choose 10 of his friends to join him on the team.
  The order in which he chooses his friends does not matter.
  This is a combination problem.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Peter wants to add 10 people to his team.
  He has 10 friends to choose from.
  The order in which he chooses his friends does not matter.
  This is a combination problem.
  The formula to calculate the number of combinations is n! / r!(n-r)!
  Where n is the total number of items to choose from, and r is the number of items to choose.
Action: Answer("C") 
  The number of ways Peter can choose 10 people from a group of 10 is 1 (all of his friends).
  Therefore, he has 1 choice.
  The number of ways Peter can choose 10 people from a group of 20 is 184,756.
  Therefore, he has 184,756 choices.
  Answer: 184,756.
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Peter wants to find 10 additional people, and he has 10 friends who would like to participate.
  This is a combination problem, because we want to find the number of ways to choose 10 people out of a group of 10.
  The formula for combinations is n choose k = n!/(k!(n-k)!), where n is the total number of items to choose from, and k is the number of items to choose.
Action: Answer("C")  
Explanation: Peter has 10 friends who would like to participate, so he needs to choose 10 people from a group of 10. Using the formula for combinations, we get 10 choose 10 = 10!/(10!(10-10)!) = 1. Therefore, Peter has only one choice for forming his team.
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  Peter wants to find 10 additional people to form a scavenger hunt team with him.
  He has 10 friends who would like to participate.
  The order in which he selects the people does not matter.
  
Solution:
  Peter needs to select 10 people from a group of 10 friends.
  This is a combination problem.
  The formula for combinations is C(n,r) = n! / (r! * (n-r)!), where n is the total number of items and r is the number of items being chosen.
  In this case, n = 10 and r = 10, since Peter needs to choose all 10 friends.
  C(10,10) = 10! / (10! * (10-10)!) = 1
  
Action: Answer("B")
Response 4:
Knowledge:
  Peter wants to choose 10 people out of 10 friends.
  The order of choosing does not matter.
  The number of combinations of n objects taken r at a time is given by the formula: C(n,r) = n!/(r!(n-r)!).
Action: Answer("C")

  He has 10 friends who would like to participate.
  The number of ways to choose k objects from a set of n objects is given by the combination formula: C(n,k) = n! / (k! * (n-k)!)

Response 6:
Knowledge:
  Peter wants to form a team of 10 additional people with 10 friends who would like to participate. 
  The order in which he selects the additional people does not matter.
  This is a combination problem, where the order of the selection does not matter and repetition is not allowed.
  The formula for combinations is nCr = n! / r!(n-r)!
  n is the total number of choices available.
  r is the number of choices to be made.
  
Action: Answer("C")  
To find the number of ways Peter can form his team, we can use the combination formula:
nCr = n! / r!(n-r)!
Peter has 10 friends who would like to participate, and he wants to choose 10 additional people to join his team. Therefore:
n = 10
r = 10
nCr = 10! / 10!(10-10)! = 10! / 10!0! = 1

  A: 10
  B: 15
  C: 18
  D: 20

  Total = Group 1 + Group 2 - Both + Neither
  Group 1 represents the number of books that belong to the first group, 
  Group 2 represents the number of books that belong to the second group, 
  Both represents the number of books that belong to both groups, 
  and Neither represents the number of books that belong to neither group. 

We can use this formula to find the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction:
  Total = 45
  Group 1 = 30
  Group 2 = 20
  Neither = Total - (Group 1 + Group 2) = 45 - (30 + 20) = 45 - 50 = -5
  Since it is not possible to have a negative number of books, this means that the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction is the size of the smaller group, which is 20.

  The ratio of the height of the electric pole to the length of its shadow is 14/10.
  We can use this ratio to find the height of the tree.
Calculation: 
  Let x be the height of the tree.
  Then we have the proportion: (x/15) = (14/10).
  Solving for x, we get: x = (15*14)/10 = 21.
Action: Answer("A")

  We can cross-multiply and solve for the height of the tree: height of the tree = (length of its shadow x height of electric pole) / length of electric pole

Question: At what price should the Karan mark a sewing machine that costs him Rs. 1200/- so that even after offering a 20% discount, he makes 20% profit?
Choices:

  B: 1,875
  C: 1,876
  D: 1,872
  E: 1,800
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  To solve the problem, we need to use the formula for profit percentage, which is:
  Profit Percentage = (Profit / Cost Price) x 100
  where Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price
  
  Let's assume that the Selling Price is SP. After offering a 20% discount, the Selling Price will be 0.8SP.
  We also know that Karan wants to make a 20% profit, which means that Profit Percentage = 20%.
  Therefore:
  20% = (SP - 1200) / 1200 x 100
  SP - 1200 = 240
  SP = 1440
  
Action: Answer("A")

  C: 2,100
  D: 2,200
  E: 1,900

Question: At a certain factory, 10 percent of the staplers produced on Monday were defective and 2 percent of the non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake. If 72 of the non-defective staplers were rejected, what was the number of staplers produced that day?
Choices:
  A: 4,000
  B: 4,200
  C: 4,500
  D: 4,800
  E: 5,000
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's say the number of staplers produced on Monday was "x".
  10 percent of the staplers produced were defective, so the number of defective staplers = 0.1x.
  The remaining staplers (non-defective staplers) = 0.9x.
  2 percent of the non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake, so the number of rejected non-defective staplers = 0.02(0.9x) = 0.018x = 72.
Action: 
  Solving the equation 0.018x = 72, we get x = 4000.
  Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the number of staplers produced on Monday is x.
  10% of the staplers produced were defective, so the number of defective staplers is 0.1x.
  The remaining staplers, which are non-defective, are (1-0.1)x = 0.9x.
  2% of the non-defective staplers were rejected by mistake, which means that 0.02(0.9x) = 0.018x staplers were rejected by mistake.
  We know that 72 non-defective staplers were rejected, so 0.018x = 72.
Action: 
  Solve for x: 
  0.018x = 72
  x = 72/0.018
  x = 4000
Answer: Answer("A")  (4,000)

  If 72 of the non-defective staplers were rejected, then 98% of non-defective staplers is equal to (100% - 2%) = 98% of (x - 10% of x).

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 12 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: M men agree to purchase a gift for Rs. D. If 3 men drop out how much more will each have to contribute towards the purchase of the gift?
Choices:
  A: D/(M-3)
  B: MD/3
  C: M/(D-3)
  D: 3D/(M2-3M)
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Initially, M men agreed to purchase a gift for Rs. D.
  After 3 men drop out, there will be M-3 men left.
  The total amount to be paid, D, will still be the same.
  We need to find out how much more each person will have to contribute towards the purchase of the gift.
  Let X be the amount that each person had to contribute initially. Then, we need to find out X + Y, where Y is the additional amount that each person has to contribute after 3 men drop out.
  We know that X = D/M.
  We need to find Y.
  Y = (D/M-3) - (D/M) = D/M - D/(M-3)
  Simplifying the above expression, we get Y = 3D/(M*(M-3)).
  Therefore, the answer is D: 3D/(M2-3M).
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Originally, M men agreed to purchase a gift for Rs. D.
  If 3 men drop out, there will now be M-3 men contributing towards the purchase of the gift.
  We need to find out how much more each person will have to contribute towards the gift.
  Let X be the amount each person had to contribute originally.
  Then, we know that M*X = D.
  After 3 men drop out, the remaining (M-3) men will need to contribute Y amount each.
  Then, we know that (M-3)*Y = D.
  We need to find out (Y-X).
  (M-3)*Y = D => Y = D/(M-3)
  X = D/M
  (Y-X) = D/(M-3) - D/M = 3D/(M(M-3))
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Initially, M men agreed to purchase a gift for Rs. D.
  After 3 men drop out, there will be M-3 men left.

  Therefore, we need to find the amount that each person will contribute after 3 men drop out.
  
Calculations:
  Initially, each person would have contributed D/M.
  After 3 men drop out, there will be M-3 men left.
  Therefore, each person will have to contribute D/(M-3).
  
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Knowledge: 
  Initially, M men agree to purchase a gift for Rs. D. 
  If 3 men drop out, then there will be M-3 men left to purchase the gift.
  Each person will have to contribute more towards the purchase of the gift.
  The total amount to be paid for the gift remains D.
  
Solution:
  Initially, each of the M men would have to contribute D/M.
  After 3 men drop out, there will be M-3 men left to share the total cost of the gift, which is still D.
  So, each of the M-3 men will have to contribute D/(M-3).
  The difference in the amount each person has to contribute is:
    D/(M-3) - D/M
    = DM/M(M-3) - D(M-3)/M(M-3)
    = (DM - D(M-3))/M(M-3)
    = 3D/(M(M-3))
Action: Answer("D")

Question: The events A and B are independent. The probability that event A occurs is 0.6, and the probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is 0.96. What is the probability that event B occurs?
Choices:
  A: 0.5
  B: 0.6
  C: 0.7
  D: 0.8
  E: 0.9
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If two events A and B are independent, then the probability of both events occurring is the product of their individual probabilities: P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B).
  The probability of at least one of the events A or B occurring is the sum of their individual probabilities minus the probability of both occurring: P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B).
  Therefore, we can use these formulas to solve the problem.
  
Calculation: 
  Let P(B) be the probability that event B occurs.
  We know that P(A) = 0.6 and P(A or B) = 0.96.
  Using the formula for P(A or B), we can write: 
  P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B)
  0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - (0.6 * P(B))
  0.96 = 0.6 + 0.4 * P(B)
  0.36 = 0.4 * P(B)
  P(B) = 0.36 / 0.4
  P(B) = 0.9
  
Answer: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - If A and B are independent events, then P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B)
  - The probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B)
  - If A and B are independent, then P(A and B) = P(A) * P(B) = 0.6 * P(B)
  
Solution:
  Let P(B) = x
  P(A or B) = 0.96
  P(A or B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A and B)
  0.96 = 0.6 + x - 0.6x
  0.36 = 0.4x
  x = 0.9

  The probability of at least one of the events A or B occurring is the complement of the probability that neither A nor B occur.
  The complement of an event A is the probability of the event "not A" occurring, which is equal to 1 minus the probability of A occurring.
  
Solution:

The probability of at least one of the events A or B occurring is the complement of the probability that neither A nor B occur: 
P(A or B) = 1 - P(not A and not B).
Since events A and B are independent, the probability that neither A nor B occur is the product of the probabilities that not A and not B occur: P(not A and not B) = P(not A) * P(not B).
The probability of not A occurring is 1 minus the probability of A occurring: P(not A) = 1 - P(A).
Therefore, we have: P(A or B) = 1 - P(not A) * P(not B) = 1 - (1 - P(A)) * (1 - P(B)).
Substituting the given values, we get: 0.96 = 1 - (1 - 0.6) * (1 - P(B)).
Simplifying this equation, we get: 0.36 = P(B) * 0.4.
Therefore, we have: P(B) = 0.36 / 0.4 = 0.9.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 16 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The price of a product is reduced by 30% . By what percentage should it be increased to make it 100%
Choices:
  A: 41.86%
  B: 42.86%
  C: 43.86%
  D: 44.86%
  E: 45.86%
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If the price of a product is reduced by x%, the new price is (100-x)% of the original price.
  If we want to increase the new price by y% to make it 100%, the new price becomes (100+y)% of the reduced price, which is equal to the original price.
  Let's use algebra to solve for y:
  If the original price is P, the new price after the 30% reduction is 0.7P.
  To find the percentage increase needed to make the new price equal to P, we need to solve the equation:
  P = (0.7P)(1 + y/100)
  Dividing both sides by 0.7P, we get:
  1 = 1.43(1 + y/100)
  Simplifying, we get:
  1 + y/100 = 1/1.43
  y/100 = (1/1.43) - 1
  y/100 = 0.3
  y = 30

Question: Two balls A and B rotate along a circular track. Ball A makes 2 full rotations in 26 minutes. Ball B makes 5 full rotation in 35 minutes. If they start rotating now from the same point, when will they be at the same starting point again?
Choices:
  A: 1 hour and 31 minutes
  B: 2 hour and 31 minutes
  C: 3 hour and 31 minutes
  D: 4 hour and 31 minutes
  E: 5 hour and 31 minutes
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The time it takes for a ball to complete one full rotation is the period of rotation.
  - Period of rotation is inversely proportional to the number of rotations in a given time.
  - When two balls meet, it means they would have completed the same number of rotations.
  - The least common multiple (LCM) of the periods of rotation of the two balls is the time it takes for them to meet again.
  - We can obtain the periods of rotation by dividing the time taken for the given number of rotations.
  
Working:
  Period of rotation of Ball A = 26 minutes / 2 = 13 minutes per rotation
  Period of rotation of Ball B = 35 minutes / 5 = 7 minutes per rotation
  LCM of 13 and 7 = 91 minutes

Question: A flagstaff 17.5 metre high casts a shadow of length 40.25 metre. The height of building, which casts a shadow of length 28.75 metre under similar conditions will be :
Choices:
  A: 12 metre
  B: 12.5 metre
  C: 13.5 metre
  D: 14 metre
  E: 15 metre
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  In similar triangles, the ratio of their corresponding sides is equal.

Then we have:
  17.5 / 40.25 = x / 28.75

  x = 17.5 * 28.75 / 40.25 = 12.5

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The ratio of the height of the flagstaff to the length of its shadow is equal to the ratio of the height of the building to the length of its shadow when the conditions are similar.
  If the flagstaff is 17.5 meters high and casts a shadow of length 40.25 meters, then the ratio of its height to the length of its shadow is 17.5/40.25 = 0.434.
  Let x be the height of the building. Then, the ratio of the height of the building to the length of its shadow is x/28.75.

  0.434 = x/28.75
  Solving for x:
  x = 0.434 * 28.75
  x = 12.47
  Rounding to the nearest 0.5 meter, we get:
Answer: ("B") 12.5 meter

  We can then solve for the height of the building using algebra.

Question: Suppose you want to arrange your English, Hindi, Mathematics, History, Geography and Science books on a shelf. In how many ways can you do it ?
Choices:
  A: 520
  B: 720
  C: 920
  D: None
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  This is a permutation problem as we are arranging books in a particular order.
  The number of permutations of n distinct objects taken r at a time is given by nPr = n!/(n-r)!, where n! represents the factorial of n.
  
Action: 
  We have 6 books to arrange in a particular order.
  Therefore, the number of ways to arrange these books is 6P6 = 6!/(6-6)! = 6!/0! = 6x5x4x3x2x1 = 720.
  Answer: Answer("B")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 20 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An exam is given in a certain class. The average (arithmetic mean) of the highest score and the lowest score is equal to x. If the average score for the entire class is equal to y and there are z students in the class, where z > 5, then in terms of x, y, and z, what is the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers?
Choices:
  A: (zy – 2x)/z
  B: (zy – 2)/z
  C: (zx – y)/(z – 2)
  D: (zy – 2x)/(z -2)
  E: (zy – x)/(z + 2)
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let H be the highest score and L be the lowest score.
  The average of the highest and lowest score is (H+L)/2.
  The average score of the entire class is the sum of the scores divided by the number of students, i.e. y = (H+L+S1+S2+...+Sn)/z, where S1, S2, ..., Sn are the scores of the remaining z-2 students.
  To find the average score excluding the highest and lowest scorers, we need to find the sum of the scores of the remaining z-2 students and divide by z-2.
  We can rewrite y as (H+L)/2 + (S1+S2+...+Sn)/z, and solve for (S1+S2+...+Sn)/z.
  (S1+S2+...+Sn)/z = y - (H+L)/2.
  We are given that (H+L)/2 = x, so (S1+S2+...+Sn)/z = y - x.
  Therefore, the average score excluding the highest and lowest scorers is (S1+S2+...+Sn)/(z-2) = [(S1+S2+...+Sn)/z] * z / (z-2) = (y-x) * z / (z-2).

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  To find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers, we need to find the sum of all the scores excluding the highest and lowest, and divide that sum by the number of students in the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers.
  If the highest and lowest scores have an average of x, then their sum is 2x.
  The sum of all the scores in the class is yz.
  Therefore, the sum of all the scores excluding the highest and lowest is yz - 2x.
  The number of students in the class excluding the highest and lowest is z - 2.
Action: Answer("D") 
Using the formula above, the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers is (yz - 2x)/(z - 2). Therefore, the answer is (D).
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Let n be the number of students in the class, and let h and l be the highest and lowest scores respectively. 
  We can use the formula for the arithmetic mean to write: (h + l)/2 = x
  The average score for the entire class is given by: (sum of all scores)/n = y
  We know that z > 5, but we do not know if z is equal to n.
  We want to find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers, which we can call A.

Approach:
  We can start by finding the sum of all scores, and then subtracting the highest and lowest scores to find the sum of the remaining scores. 
  We can then divide by the number of remaining students to find the average score. 
  To do this, we need to express the sum of all scores in terms of x, y, and z.

Solution:
  Let S be the sum of all scores, and let A' be the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers. 
  We have: 
  S = y * n
  h + l = 2x
  A' = (S - h - l)/(n - 2) = (S - 2x)/(n - 2)
  We can express S in terms of z by using the fact that z > 5:
  S = y * n = y * (z + n - z) = yz + yn - yz = yn + y(z - 1)
  Substituting this into the expression for A', we get:
  A' = (yn + y(z - 1) - 2x)/(n - 2)
  = (y(n - 2) + yz - 2x)/(n - 2)
  = (zy - 2x)/(z - 2)
  Therefore, the answer is (D) (zy - 2x)/(z - 2).
Response 3:
Knowledge: 
  Let A be the highest score and let B be the lowest score. 
  The average of A and B is (A + B)/2.
  The average of the entire class is the sum of all scores divided by the number of students.
  The sum of all scores is (A + B) + (sum of all scores excluding A and B).
  z > 5 means that there are at least 3 students in the class besides the highest and lowest scorers.
  
Solution:
  Let C be the sum of all scores excluding A and B.
  We know that (A + B)/2 = x, which means that A + B = 2x.
  We also know that (A + B + C)/z = y, which means that A + B + C = yz.
  We can substitute A + B = 2x into the second equation to get 2x + C = yz.
  We can solve for C to get C = yz - 2x.
  The average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers is C/(z - 2).
  Substituting C = yz - 2x, we get the average score is (yz - 2x)/(z - 2).
Action: Answer("D")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 24 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of her rectangular yard and leave one side of 10 meters unfenced. If the yard has an area of 240 square meters, how many meters of fencing does she need?
Choices:
  A: 58
  B: 62
  C: 66
  D: 70
  E: 74
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The area of a rectangle can be calculated by multiplying its length by its width.
  - The perimeter of a rectangle can be calculated by adding twice its length to twice its width.
  
Let the length of the rectangular yard be L and the width be W. We know that:

1. L x W = 240  (since the area of the yard is 240 square meters)
2. L + 2W = 30  (since three sides are fenced and one side of 10 meters is not fenced)

We can solve for L in equation 2 and substitute into equation 1 to solve for W:

L = 30 - 2W
(30 - 2W) x W = 240
2W^2 - 30W + 240 = 0
W^2 - 15W + 120 = 0
(W - 8)(W - 15) = 0

Therefore, W = 8 or W = 15. If W = 8, then L = 7.5, which does not make sense since the length should be longer than the width. Therefore, W = 15 and L = 16. The amount of fencing needed is:

Fencing = 2L + W = 2(16) + 15 = 47 meters.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The area of a rectangle is calculated as length * width.
  - Alice has a rectangular yard, and she wants to fence three sides, which means the unfenced side is opposite to one of the fenced sides.
  - If we let x be the length of the yard, then the width is 240/x.
  - Alice needs to fence three sides, which are two lengths and one width. The length of the unfenced side is given as 10 meters.
  - The total length of fencing required is the sum of the lengths of the three fenced sides.
  - We can use the formula: Length of fencing = 2 * length + width
  
Calculation:
  - Let's find the length of the yard.
  - Area = length * width
  - 240 = length * (240/length)
  - length^2 = 240 * (240/length)
  - length^2 = 57600/length
  - length^3 = 57600
  - length = cuberoot(57600)
  - length = 24
  - The width of the yard is 240/24 = 10.
  - The length of fencing required is 2*24 + 10 = 58.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  The area of a rectangle can be found by multiplying its length and width.
  If Alice leaves one side of 10 meters unfenced, then she needs to fence the other three sides.
  The perimeter of a rectangle can be found by adding up the lengths of all its sides.
  Let L be the length of the rectangle and W be its width. We know that L * W = 240 and L + W + L = perimeter - 10.
Action: 
  We can solve for L and W by using the first equation: L = 240 / W. 
  We can substitute L in the second equation to get: (240 / W) + W + (240 / W) = perimeter - 10. 
  Simplifying the equation, we get: perimeter = 2W + (480 / W) + 10.
  To minimize the perimeter, we need to find the value of W that makes the expression 2W + (480 / W) as small as possible. 
  We can do this by taking the derivative of the expression with respect to W, setting it equal to zero, and solving for W. 
  The derivative is: 2 - (480 / W^2), which equals zero when W^2 = 240. 
  Therefore, W = sqrt(240) = 4 * sqrt(15).
  Substituting this value back into the expression for the perimeter, we get: perimeter = 2(4 * sqrt(15)) + (480 / (4 * sqrt(15))) + 10 = 58. 
  Therefore, Alice needs 58 meters of fencing.
Answer: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  - The formula for the area of a rectangle is length x width.
  - Alice wants to fence three sides of the yard.
  - One side of the yard is already 10 meters long.
  
Solution:
  Let's assume the length of the yard is L and the width of the yard is W.
  From the question, we know that:
  - L x W = 240 (the area of the yard)
  - One side of the yard is 10 meters long.
  
  We want to find out how much fencing Alice needs for the other three sides.
  The other three sides are:
  - Two sides with length L
  - One side with length W
  
  The total length of fencing needed is:
  - 2L + W
  
  We can use the equation for the area of the yard to solve for one of the variables.
  W = 240 / L
  
  We can substitute this into the equation for the total length of fencing needed.
  2L + (240 / L) = length of fencing needed
  
  We can take the derivative of this equation and set it to zero to find the minimum value of length of fencing needed.
  After solving the equation, we get L = 12.
  
  We can now substitute this value of L into the equation for the total length of fencing needed.
  2L + W = 2 x 12 + (240 / 12) = 24 + 20 = 44
  
  Therefore, Alice needs 44 meters of fencing.
  
Action: Answer("E")

Knowledge:
  - A rectangular yard has opposite sides with the same length.
  - The formula for the area of a rectangle is length x width.
  - Alice wants to fence three sides of the yard, which are the two lengths and one of the widths.
  - The other width of the yard does not need to be fenced.
  - The perimeter of a rectangle is the sum of the lengths of all sides.
  
Solution:
  - Let's call the width of the yard "w" and the length of the yard "l".
  - We know that the area of the yard is 240 square meters, so we have the equation w x l = 240.
  - We also know that Alice wants to fence three sides of the yard, which are the two lengths (l) and one of the widths (w), so the length of fencing she needs is l + l + w = 2l + w.
  - We are given that one of the widths is 10 meters, so we can substitute w = 10 into the equation w x l = 240 to get l = 24.
  - Therefore, the length of fencing Alice needs is 2l + w = 2(24) + 10 = 58 meters.

Response 5:
Knowledge: 
  The area of a rectangle is given by the formula A = length × width.
  The perimeter of a rectangle is given by the formula P = 2(length + width).
  
Let's call the length of the rectangular yard "L" and the width "W". 

We know that the area of the yard is 240 square meters, so we have:

L × W = 240

We also know that Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of the yard, so she needs to fence the two lengths and one width. The length of fencing required for the two lengths is 2L and the length of fencing required for the width is W - 10 (since one side is already unfenced). So the total length of fencing required is:

2L + W - 10

We can also use the formula for the perimeter of a rectangle to express one of the variables in terms of the other. Solving for L, we get:

L = (240/W)

Substituting this into the expression for the length of fencing required, we get:

2(240/W) + W - 10

Simplifying this expression, we get:

480/W + W - 10

Now we need to find the value of W that minimizes this expression. We can do this by taking the derivative and setting it equal to zero:

d/dW (480/W + W - 10) = -480/W^2 + 1 = 0

Solving for W, we get:

W = sqrt(480)

Plugging this value of W back into the expression for the length of fencing required, we get:

2(240/sqrt(480)) + sqrt(480) - 10 ≈ 62.02

Question: A sporting goods store carries only yellow and white golf balls. If the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, and in doing so sold all of its white golf balls, how many yellow golf balls did the store have to begin the day?
Choices:
  A: 80
  B: 120
  C: 240
  D: 320
  E: 360
Response 0:

  - The store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, so the number of white golf balls sold is half of 480, which is 240.
  - The store sold all of its white golf balls, so none were left at the end of the day.
  - Therefore, the number of yellow golf balls left at the end of the day is 480-240=240.

Topic: Math
Question: The bus fare for two persons for travelling between Agra and Aligarh id four-thirds the train fare between the same places for one person. The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train between the two places is Rs.1512. Find the train fare between the two places for one person?
Choices:
  A: 126
  B: 77
  C: 88
  D: 66
  E: 54
Response 0:
Let's assume the train fare for one person be Rs. x. 
Then, the bus fare for two persons would be Rs. (4/3)x. 

Total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus = 6 × (4/3)x = 8x
Total fare paid by 8 persons travelling by train = 8x

Given, the sum of the total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train is Rs. 1512. Therefore:

8x + 6 × (4/3)x = 1512
Simplifying the above equation, we get:
x = 126

Thus, the train fare between the two places for one person is Rs. 126.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Let the train fare between the two places for one person be x.
Then, the bus fare for two persons between the same places is (4/3)x.
The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus is (6/2) * (4/3)x = 8x.
The total fare paid by 8 persons travelling by train is 8x.
The total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train is 8x + 8x = 16x.
Given that the total fare paid by 6 persons travelling by bus and 8 persons travelling by train is Rs.1512.
Therefore, 16x = 1512.
Hence, x = 94.5.
Therefore, the train fare between the two places for one person is Rs.94.5.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 27 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Jim filled his dog's bowl with dog food. Starting at 8:00 am, Jim's dog ate exactly once an hour, consuming exactly 1/3 of the dog food remaining in the bowl at each feeding session. Approximately, what percent of the original food was in the dog's bowl right before the dog began to eat at noon of the same day?
Choices:
  A: 20%
  B: 25%
  C: 30%
  D: 35%
  E: 40%
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Jim's dog ate every hour from 8:00 am until 12:00 pm, so the dog ate four times.
  At each feeding session, the dog ate 1/3 of the remaining dog food.
Action: Answer("E")  

Let F be the original amount of dog food in the bowl, then the amount of dog food remaining after the first feeding session (i.e., at 9:00 am) is (2/3)F. Similarly, the amount of dog food remaining after the second feeding session (i.e., at 10:00 am) is (2/3)(2/3)F = (4/9)F. Continuing this process, the amount of dog food remaining after the third feeding session (i.e., at 11:00 am) is (2/3)(4/9)F = (8/27)F, and the amount of dog food remaining after the fourth feeding session (i.e., at 12:00 pm) is (2/3)(8/27)F = (16/81)F.

Therefore, the ratio of the amount of dog food remaining at noon to the original amount of dog food is (16/81)F / F = 16/81. To convert this to a percentage, we multiply by 100 to get (16/81) * 100% = 19.75%, which is approximately 20%. However, this is not one of the available answer choices. The closest answer choice is E: 40%, which is double the correct answer. This is because at each feeding session, the amount of dog food remaining in the bowl is reduced by 1/3, which is a relatively large amount. Therefore, the percentage of dog food remaining decreases rapidly, and by noon, only about 20% of the original dog food is left in the bowl.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Each hour, the dog eats 1/3 of the remaining food in the bowl.
  The dog starts eating at 8:00 am and eats four times, so the dog eats at 9:00 am, 10:00 am, 11:00 am, and 12:00 pm.
  We want to find the percent of the original food remaining in the bowl at 12:00 pm.
  
Solution:
  Let's assume that the original amount of food in the bowl is 100 units.
  At 9:00 am, the dog eats 1/3 of the remaining 100 units, which is 33.33 units, leaving 66.67 units.
  At 10:00 am, the dog eats 1/3 of the remaining 66.67 units, which is 22.22 units, leaving 44.45 units.
  At 11:00 am, the dog eats 1/3 of the remaining 44.45 units, which is 14.82 units, leaving 29.63 units.
  At 12:00 pm, the dog eats 1/3 of the remaining 29.63 units, which is 9.88 units, leaving 19.75 units.
  
  Therefore, the percent of the original food remaining in the bowl at 12:00 pm is 19.75%.

Topic: Math
Question: Anna is able to buy 5 more articles for $300 after the price of each article decreased by 15%. What is the new selling price of each article?
Choices:
  A: $8
  B: $10
  C: $13.6
  D: $22.9
  E: $40
Response 0:
Knowledge:
- Anna can buy 5 more articles for $300, which means each article costs 300/5 = $60.
- The price of each article decreased by 15%. This means the new price of each article is 85% of the original price.

Calculation:
- Let x be the original selling price of each article.
- 85% of x is 0.85x.
- We know that 0.85x * 5 + 5x = 300 (the total cost of 5 more articles and the original articles is $300).
- Solving this equation, we get x = $13.6.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - "Price decreased by 15%" means the new price is 85% of the original price.
  - Anna was able to buy 5 more articles for $300, which means each article costs $60 ($300/5).
  - If the price of each article decreased by 15%, the new price can be calculated as follows: new price = 85% * original price.

Action: 
  - Calculate the original price of each article: $60 / 85% = $70.59 (rounded to the nearest cent).
  - Calculate the new price of each article: 85% * $70.59 = $60.
  - The new selling price of each article is $60.
  - Answer("None of the above")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  1. Anna is buying a certain number of articles.
  2. The original price of each article has decreased by 15%.
  3. Anna can now buy 5 more articles for $300.
  4. We need to find the new selling price of each article.

Let the original price of each article be x.
After the 15% discount, the new price of each article will be 0.85x.

Anna can now buy 5 more articles for $300, so she must have been able to buy (5+x) articles for the original price.
The total amount that Anna would have needed to buy (5+x) articles at the original price is given by (5+x)*x = 5x + x^2.

We know that Anna can buy (5+x) articles for $300, so (5+x)*0.85x = 300.
Solving for x gives x = 10.

Therefore, the new selling price of each article is 0.85x = 0.85*10 = $8.50.

  Anna is able to buy 5 more articles after the price of each article decreased by 15%.
  The total cost of the new articles is $300.
  We need to find the new selling price of each article.

Action: Answer("C")
Solution:
  Let x be the original selling price of one article.
  After the 15% decrease, the new selling price of one article is 0.85x.
  Anna is able to buy 5 more articles, so she can buy a total of (5+x) articles.
  The total cost of the new articles is $300, so we can write the equation:
  0.85x(5+x) = $300
  4.25x + 0.85x^2 = $300
  0.85x^2 + 4.25x - $300 = 0
  Solving the quadratic equation using the quadratic formula, we get:
  x = (-4.25 ± sqrt(4.25^2 + 4*0.85*300)) / (2*0.85)
  x = (-4.25 ± sqrt(1405)) / 1.7
  Since x must be positive, we take the positive root:
  x = (-4.25 + sqrt(1405)) / 1.7 ≈ $13.6
  Therefore, the new selling price of each article is approximately $13.6.

Simplifying the equation:

y = 13.6 (rounded to one decimal place) since the other root is negative.
Therefore, the new selling price of each article is $13.6.

Question: A rope 20 meters long is cut into two pieces. If the length of one piece of rope is 3 meters shorter than the length of the other, what is the length, in meters, of the longer piece of rope?
Choices:
  A: 7.5
  B: 8.9
  C: 9.9
  D: 11.5
  E: 11.7
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let x be the length of the longer piece of rope. Then the length of the shorter piece of rope is x-3, since the length of one piece is 3 meters shorter than the length of the other. We know that the sum of the lengths of the two pieces is 20 meters. Therefore, we can write an equation: x + (x-3) = 20. If we solve for x, we can find the length of the longer piece.
  A: 7.5 is not a solution to the equation x + (x-3) = 20. 
  B: 8.9 is not a solution to the equation x + (x-3) = 20. 
  C: 9.9 is not a solution to the equation x + (x-3) = 20. 
  D: 11.5 is a solution to the equation x + (x-3) = 20, since 11.5 + 8.5 = 20. 
  E: 11.7 is not a solution to the equation x + (x-3) = 20. 
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let x be the length of the longer piece of rope.
  The length of the shorter piece of rope is then x - 3.
  The sum of the lengths of the two pieces of rope is 20 meters.
  Therefore, x + (x - 3) = 20.
  Solving for x, we get x = 11.5.
  Therefore, the length of the longer piece of rope is 11.5 meters.

Topic: Math
Question: In a survey of students, each student selected from a list of 10 songs the 2 songs that the student liked best. If each song was selected 5 times, how many students were surveyed?
Choices:
  A: 96
  B: 48
  C: 32
  D: 25
  E: 18
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If each song was selected 5 times, and each student selected 2 songs, then there were 2/5 = 0.4 of a student for each song.
  The total number of students surveyed is the number of units of 0.4 that add up to a whole number.
  A: 96 = 240/2.5, which means that 240 songs were selected, but this is not divisible by 10, so this is not the answer.
  B: 48 = 120/2.5, which means that 120 songs were selected, and this is divisible by 10, so this could be the answer.
  C: 32 = 80/2.5, which means that 80 songs were selected, but this is not divisible by 10, so this is not the answer.
  D: 25 = 62.5/2.5, which means that 62.5 songs were selected, but this is not divisible by 10, so this is not the answer.
  E: 18 = 45/2.5, which means that 45 songs were selected, but this is not divisible by 10, so this is not the answer.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Each student selects 2 songs from a list of 10 songs. This means that each pair of songs is selected twice.
  If each song was selected 5 times, then there were a total of 10*5=50 selections made.
  Since each pair of songs is selected twice, the total number of pairs of songs selected is 50/2=25.
  The number of ways to choose 2 songs from a list of 10 is 10 choose 2 = 45.
  The number of students surveyed is equal to the number of pairs of songs selected divided by the number of ways to choose 2 songs from a list of 10.
Calculation:
  Number of students = 25 / 45 = 5/9 of a student per pair of songs.
  Since we cannot have a fraction of a student, the nearest whole number of students surveyed is 1. Therefore, the answer is A: 96. 
Action: Answer("A")

  Therefore, there were a total of 2N song selections made by all students. 
  We can set up an equation: 2N = 50
  Solving for N: N = 25

Let's assume that there were N students surveyed. Each student selected 2 songs, so the total number of song selections made by the students is also:
  Total number of song selections = 2 selections per student * N students = 2N

We can equate the two expressions for the total number of song selections and solve for N:
  50 = 2N
  N = 25

Question: The original retail price of an appliance was 60 percent more than its wholesale cost. If the appliance was actually sold for 20 percent less than the original retail price, then it was sold for what percent more than its wholesale cost?
Choices:
  A: 20%
  B: 28%
  C: 36%
  D: 40%
  E: 42%
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let W be the wholesale cost of the appliance.
  The original retail price of the appliance was 60% more than W, which is 1.6W.
  The appliance was sold for 20% less than its original retail price, which is 0.8(1.6W) = 1.28W.
  The question is asking for the percentage that 1.28W is greater than W.
  This is equivalent to asking for the percentage increase from W to 1.28W.
  The percentage increase from W to X is (X-W)/W * 100%.
  
Action: Answer("B")  
To find the answer, we need to calculate the percentage increase from W to 1.28W:
  Percentage increase = (1.28W - W)/W * 100% = 0.28W/W * 100% = 28%
Therefore, the appliance was sold for 28% more than its wholesale cost. The answer is (B).

Topic: Math
Question: When folded into two equal halves a rectangular sheet had a perimeter of 48cm for each part folded along one set of sides and the same is 66cm when folded along the other set of sides. Find the area of the sheet.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 1120
  C: 792
  D: 1320
  E: 1200
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The perimeter of a rectangle is given by the formula P = 2(l+w), where l and w are the length and width of the rectangle, respectively.
  When a rectangle is folded into two equal halves along its length, the width of each part becomes half of the original width, while the length remains the same. Therefore, the perimeter becomes P = 2(l+w/2) = 2l+w, where w/2 is the new width.
  Similarly, when a rectangle is folded into two equal halves along its width, the length of each part becomes half of the original length, while the width remains the same. Therefore, the perimeter becomes P = 2(l/2+w) = l+2w, where l/2 is the new length.
  We can solve a system of equations to find the length and width of the rectangle, and then calculate its area using the formula A = lw.

Action: Answer("D") 

Let l be the length and w be the width of the rectangle.
From the given information, we have the system of equations:
2l + w = 48
l + 2w = 66
Solving this system, we get l = 18 and w = 15.
Therefore, the area of the rectangle is A = lw = 18*15 = 270.
When folded, each part has dimensions 18 x 7.5 and 9 x 15, respectively.
Thus, the area of the sheet is 2A = 2*270 = 540 cm².

Knowledge:
- The perimeter of a rectangle is the sum of all its sides.
- When a rectangle is folded in half along one set of sides, the perimeter of each part is half of the original perimeter.
- The area of a rectangle is the product of its length and width.

Let x be the length of the rectangle and y be the width.
We know that 2(x+y) = 48 when folded along one set of sides, or x+y = 24.
We also know that 2(x+y) = 66 when folded along the other set of sides, or x+y = 33.

Solving for x and y, we get x = 15 and y = 9.
The area of the rectangle is xy = 15*9 = 135.

So B = 18cm.
Substituting this into the first equation gives: L + 36 = 48
So L = 12cm.

The area of the rectangle is given by the formula A = L*B, so:
A = 12*18 = 216 sq.cm

Topic: Math
Question: On a normal day Bill usually averages about 15 mph when riding his bicycle. On a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph. How far can Bill travel on a windy day in 21 minutes? Round to the nearest hundredth.
Choices:
  A: 2 miles
  B: 2.25 miles
  C: 3.25 miles
  D: 3.85 miles
  E: 2.85 miles
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If Bill averages 15 mph for x hours, then he can travel d = 15x miles.
  If his speed is reduced by 4 mph, then his effective speed is 15-4 = 11 mph.
  If he travels at 11 mph for t hours, then he can travel d = 11t miles.
  21 minutes is 21/60 = 0.35 hours.
Solution:
  On a windy day, Bill's speed is 11 mph.
  In 21 minutes, he can travel d = 11(0.35) = 3.85 miles.
  Rounding to the nearest hundredth, the answer is approximately 3.85.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Distance = Speed × Time
  Bill's speed on a normal day is 15 mph.
  On a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph, so his speed will be 15 - 4 = 11 mph.
  The time given is 21 minutes.

Calculation:
  Distance = Speed × Time
  Distance = 11 miles/hour × (21/60) hour
  Distance = 3.85 miles

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 34 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In a bag of red and green sweets, the ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4. If the bag contains 120 green sweets, how many red sweets are there?
Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 80
  C: 95
  D: 100
  E: 85
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4.
  This means that for every 3 red sweets, there are 4 green sweets.
  We know that there are 120 green sweets in the bag.
  
Calculation:
  If the ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4, then the total ratio is 3+4=7.
  We can use the ratio to find out how many red sweets there are:
  If there are 4 green sweets for every 7 sweets, then there are 3 red sweets for every 7 sweets.
  So, if there are 120 green sweets, then there are (3/7)*120 = 51.43 red sweets in the bag.
  However, we cannot have a fraction of a sweet, so we need to round this number to the nearest whole number.
  
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  1. The ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4.
  2. The bag contains 120 green sweets.
  
Solution:
  1. Let's assume that the number of red sweets in the bag is 3x (since the ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4).
  2. Also, we know that the number of green sweets in the bag is 4x (since the ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4).
  3. We are given that the bag contains 120 green sweets. So, we can form an equation: 4x = 120, which gives us x = 30.
  4. Now we can find the number of red sweets: 3x = 3 * 30 = 90.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  The ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4.
  This means that for every 3 red sweets there are 4 green sweets.
  We are given that there are 120 green sweets in the bag.
  
Calculation:
  Let's use the ratio to determine the number of red sweets in the bag:
  3/4 = x/120
  Cross-multiplying, we get:
  4x = 3 * 120
  4x = 360
  x = 90
  
Action: Answer("A")

  - The ratio of red sweets to green sweets is 3:4.

    3/4 = r/120
  - To solve for "r", we can cross-multiply and simplify:
    4r = 3 * 120
    4r = 360
    r = 90
  - Therefore, there are 90 red sweets.

  If for every 4 green sweets there are 3 red sweets, then for every 1 green sweet there are 3/4 red sweets.
  To find the number of red sweets, we can multiply the number of green sweets by the ratio of red sweets to green sweets.
  Number of red sweets = 120 * (3/4) = 90
Answer: Answer("A")

  3/4 = x/120
  where x is the number of red sweets.
  To solve for x, we can cross-multiply and simplify:
  3 * 120 = 4 * x
  360 = 4x
  x = 90

Let's solve the equation now. 
Total amount collected = Amount each person was supposed to pay x Number of people
So, (96 + 4x - 16) = x * y, where y is the number of people who actually attended the picnic.
4x + 80 = xy
4(x+20) = y(x)
So, y = 4(x+20)/x
Now, we need to find an integer value of x, such that y is also an integer. 
A: 8, B: 12, C: 16, D: 24, E: 25

If we substitute x = 12, y = 8/3, which is not an integer.
If we substitute x = 16, y = 5, which is an integer.
If we substitute x = 24, y = 3.33, which is not an integer.
If we substitute x = 25, y = 4, which is an integer.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 38 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Two cars are travelling from the same starting point in the same direction, having started their commute at the same time. The first car travels at a steady rate of 55 mph, while the second travels at a steady rate of 52 mph. How much time will pass before the cars are 15 miles away from each other?
Choices:
  A: 3 hours
  B: 5 hours
  C: 6 hours
  D: 4 hours
  E: 7 hours
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The rate of the first car is 55 mph, meaning it travels 55 miles in one hour.
  The rate of the second car is 52 mph, meaning it travels 52 miles in one hour.
  If the two cars are moving in the same direction, the distance between them will increase at a rate equal to the difference in their speeds. 
  We want to find the time it takes for the distance between them to be 15 miles.
  We can use the formula: time = distance / rate
  
Calculation:
  Let's call the time it takes for the distance between the two cars to be 15 miles "t".
  In that time, the first car will travel 55t miles.
  In that same time, the second car will travel 52t miles.
  The distance between them will be the difference between the distances they travel: 55t - 52t = 3t.
  We want to find the time it takes for the distance between them to be 15 miles: 3t = 15
  Solving for t: t = 5
  
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The relative speed between the two cars is the difference between their speeds, which is 55 mph - 52 mph = 3 mph.

  B: 24
  C: 48
  D: 20
  E: 36

Action: Answer("48")

Knowledge:
  The man wants to have fruit for breakfast and vegetable for dinner.
  He has 6 different types of fruit and 8 different types of vegetables.
  He can only eat one type at a time.
  The number of ways to eat breakfast and dinner can be calculated by multiplying the number of ways he can choose fruit for breakfast by the number of ways he can choose vegetable for dinner.
  The number of ways to choose k items from n different items can be calculated by the formula nCk = n! / (k! * (n-k)!).
Action: 
  The number of ways to choose fruit for breakfast is 6C1 = 6.
  The number of ways to choose vegetable for dinner is 8C1 = 8.
  The number of ways to eat breakfast and dinner is 6 * 8 = 48.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 41 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: While selling a watch, a shopkeeper gives a discount of 5%. If he gives a discount of 7%, he earns Rs. 15 less as profit. The marked price of the watch is:
Choices:
  A: Rs. 697.50
  B: Rs. 712.50
  C: Rs. 787.50
  D: Rs. 750
  E: Rs. 780
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let the marked price of the watch be M.
  The shopkeeper gave a discount of 5%, which means the selling price (S) is 95% of the marked price (M).
  The shopkeeper earned a profit (P) on the sale of the watch, which is the difference between the selling price and the cost price (C).
  If the shopkeeper gives a discount of 7%, the selling price (S') is 93% of the marked price (M).
  If the shopkeeper gives a discount of 7%, the profit (P') is Rs. 15 less than the profit earned with a discount of 5%.
  We can set up the following equations to solve for M:
    S = 0.95M
    P = S - C
    S' = 0.93M
    P' = S' - C = P - 15

Action: Answer("C")  
To solve for M, we can use substitution and algebraic manipulation:
  S = 0.95M
  C = S - P
  S' = 0.93M
  P' = P - 15
  S' - C = P'
  0.93M - (S - P) = P - 15
  0.93M - 0.95M + P = P - 15
  -0.02M = -15
  M = 750
Therefore, the marked price of the watch is Rs. 787.50. Answer: ("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let the marked price of the watch be M.
  The shopkeeper gives a 5% discount, which means the customer pays 95% of the marked price. So the selling price is 0.95M.
  If the shopkeeper gives a 7% discount, the customer pays 93% of the marked price. So the selling price is 0.93M.
  The difference between the selling prices when giving a 5% and a 7% discount is Rs. 15.
  So, 0.95M - 0.93M = 15
  0.02M = 15
  M = 750
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  Let the marked price of the watch be M and the cost price be C.
  When the shopkeeper gives a discount of 5%, he earns a profit P1 such that:
  P1 = M * 0.95 - C
  When the shopkeeper gives a discount of 7%, he earns a profit P2 such that:
  P2 = M * 0.93 - C
  We are also given that P1 - P2 = 15.
  We can use these equations to solve for M.
Calculation:
  P1 - P2 = (M * 0.95 - C) - (M * 0.93 - C) = M * 0.02 = 15
  M = 15 / 0.02 = 750

  Thus, if the profit decreases by Rs. 15 when the discount is increased by 2%, the profit at 5% discount is Rs. 30 less than the profit at no discount.
  This means that the profit earned by the shopkeeper at 5% discount is less than the profit at no discount by Rs. 30.
  Profit% = (Profit/Cost Price) × 100%
  Cost Price = Selling Price × (100 / (100 - Profit%))
  Selling Price = (100 - Discount%) × M / 100

  0.95M - C = 0.93M - C - 15
  0.02M = 15
  M = 750

Question: I have a money pouch containing Rs. 700. There are equal number of 25 paise coins, 50 paise coins and one rupee coins.
How many of each are there?
Choices:
  A: 453
  B: 651
  C: 400
  D: 487
  E: 286
Response 0:
Let's try solving this problem step by step:
- Let's assume that there are 'x' coins of each denomination (25 paise, 50 paise, and 1 rupee).
- The total value of 25 paise coins = 0.25 * 0.01 * x = 0.0025 * x rupees
- The total value of 50 paise coins = 0.50 * 0.01 * x = 0.005 * x rupees
- The total value of 1 rupee coins = 1 * x = 1 * x rupees
- The total value of all the coins = 0.0025x + 0.005x + x = 1.0075x rupees
- As per the question, the total value of all the coins is equal to Rs. 700
- Therefore, 1.0075x = 700
- Solving for x, we get x = 694.7 (approx.)
- As the number of coins cannot be in decimal, we can assume that there are 694 coins of each denomination.
- Therefore, the answer is:
  - Number of 25 paise coins = 694
  - Number of 50 paise coins = 694
  - Number of 1 rupee coins = 694
- This means we have a total of (694*3)= 2082 coins.

Action: Answer("E")

1.75x = 700
x = 400
Therefore, there are 400 coins of each type.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 43 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. It costs Rs.260 to paper the walls of the room with paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter allowing an area of 15 sq.m for doors and windows. The height of the room is:
Choices:
  A: 2.6m
  B: 3.9m
  C: 4m
  D: 4.2m
  E: 4.4m
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  1. The semi-perimeter of a room is half of the sum of the lengths of its four walls.
  2. The height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5 means that the height is 2x and the semi-perimeter is 5x.
  3. The cost of papering the walls is Rs.260, with paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter, and an area of 15 sq.m is deducted for doors and windows.

Calculation:
Let x be the common ratio and h be the height of the room.
Then, the semi-perimeter of the room is 5x, and the length of each wall is 5x/2.
The total area of the walls is 2h(5x/2) = 5hx square meters.
The cost of papering the walls is (5hx)(2/Rs.100)m = hx/10 Rs.
The area of the doors and windows is 15 sq.m, so the total area to be papered is 5hx - 15 sq.m.
Therefore, hx/10 = (5hx - 15) (50/100) Rs.
Solving for x, we get x = 3.
Therefore, the height of the room is 2x = 6 meters.

Action: Answer("None of the Above") 

None of the above options matches the calculated height of the room which is 6 meters.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  1. Semi-perimeter = (Perimeter of Room)/2
  2. Cost of papering the walls = Cost per meter x length of paper used
  3. Area of the room = height x Semi-perimeter x 2
  4. Area of doors and windows = 15 sq.m
  
Let the height of the room be 2x and the semi-perimeter be 5x.

Then, the perimeter of the room = 2(2x + 5x) = 14x

Length of paper used = Perimeter of room x Height of room = 14x x 2x = 28x^2

Cost of papering the walls = 2 x (28x^2/100) x 260 = 1456x^2

Area of the room = 2x x 5x x 2 = 20x^2

Area of doors and windows = 15 sq.m

Therefore, area of the walls = 20x^2 - 15

Length of paper used = area of walls / width of paper = (20x^2 - 15) / 0.5 = 40x^2 - 30

Equating the two expressions for length of paper used, we get:

40x^2 - 30 = 28x^2

12x^2 = 30

x^2 = 2.5

x = 1.58 (approx.)

Therefore, the height of the room = 2x = 2(1.58) = 3.16 m (approx.)

Action: Answer("None of the above") 

(Note: The correct answer is not one of the given choices. The height of the room is approximately 3.16 meters, which is not one of the given options.)
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  The semi-perimeter of a room is half of the sum of the room's four walls.
  The cost of papering the walls of a room is the product of the perimeter of the room and the cost per unit length of the wallpaper.
  To find the height of the room, we need to use the ratio of the height to the semi-perimeter.

Action: Answer("C") 

Let the height of the room be 2x and the semi-perimeter be 5x. 
Then, the perimeter of the room is 10x. 

The area of the doors and windows is 15 sq.m, so the area of the walls is (10x * h) - 15. 

The cost of papering the walls is Rs. 260, which is equal to (0.5 * 50/1000 * (10x * h - 15)) * 2. 
Simplifying this expression, we get:
  0.01 * (10x * h - 15) = 2.6
  10x * h - 15 = 260
  10x * h = 275

Using the ratio of height to semi-perimeter, we can write:
  h / (5x) = 2/5
  h = 2x
  
Substituting for h in the previous equation, we get:
  10x * 2x = 275
  20x^2 = 275
  x^2 = 13.75
  x = sqrt(13.75)
  
Therefore, the height of the room is:
  h = 2x = 2 * sqrt(13.75) = 4.15 ≈ 4m
  
So, the answer is C.

     - 2x / 5y = 2/5 => x = 2y
     - Cost of papering the walls = Area of the walls x Cost of paper per unit area
     - Area of the walls = (Perimeter of the room x Height of the room) - Area of doors and windows
Action:

  2. Let Length = L and Breadth = B, then we have:
     - 2x / 5 (L + B) = 2/5 => x = (L + B) / 2
     - Area of doors and windows = 15 sq.m

     - Area of the walls = 5xL + 5xB - 15
     - Cost of papering the walls = 5(L + B) x Height x 2 + Cost of doors and windows
     - Cost of doors and windows = 15 x 2 = 30
     - Cost of papering the walls = 10(L + B)x + 30
     - Given: Cost of papering the walls = Rs. 260 and Cost of paper per unit area = Rs. 2/m
  3. Solving for L and B in terms of x, we get:
     - L = 5x/3 and B = 5x/3
  4. Substituting the values of L and B in terms of x in the equation for cost of papering the walls, we get:
     - 10(5x/3) x + 30 = 260
     - x = 4.2m

Response 4:
Knowledge:
  1. "Semi-perimeter" is half of the perimeter of a polygon.
  2. "Rs." is the symbol for Indian Rupee, the currency of India.
  3. To paper the walls of the room, we need to find the perimeter of the room.
  4. The cost of the papering job is equal to the cost of the paper multiplied by the length of the paper required to cover the walls.
  5. The area of the doors and windows needs to be subtracted from the total area of the walls to obtain the area of the walls to be papered.
  6. The height of the room can be found using the ratio of the height to the semi-perimeter.

Solution:
Let the height of the room be 2x and the semi-perimeter be 5x.
Then, the perimeter of the room is 10x.
Let the length of the room be L.
Then, 10xL = Area of the walls to be papered + Area of doors and windows
            = 2xL + 2(5x)(L/2) + 15
            = 2xL + 5xL + 15
            = 7xL + 15
Therefore, L = (10xL - 15)/7x
The length of the paper required to cover the walls is L + 0.5m on top and bottom.
Thus, the cost of papering the walls is 2(L + 0.5)(10x) = 20x(L+0.5)
Substituting L in terms of x, we get:
Cost = 20x(((10x(10x-15))/(7x))+0.5)
         = 200x((10x-15)/(7x)+0.5)
         = 4000/7(x^2) + 200x - 600/7
         = 4000/7(x^2) + 200x - 85.71
Given that the cost of papering is Rs.260, we have:
4000/7(x^2) + 200x - 85.71 = 260
4000/7(x^2) + 200x = 345.71
(x^2) + (35/8)x - 86.4286 = 0
Using the quadratic formula, we get:
x = 4.2 or x = -20.547
Since the height of the room cannot be negative, the height of the room is 2x = 8.4 m.
Therefore, the answer is D: 4.2m.

Response 5:
Knowledge:
  1. The semi-perimeter of a room is half the sum of the lengths of all its walls.
  2. The cost of papering a wall is the product of the length of the wall and the cost per meter of the paper.
  3. The area of a rectangular door or window is the product of its length and height.
  4. The height of the room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5 means that the ratio of the height to half the sum of the lengths of all the walls is 2:5.
  
Solution:
Let the height of the room be 2x and the sum of the lengths of all the walls be 2y. Then we have:
2x : 5y = 2 : 5
10x = 2(2y)
5x = y

Let the length, width, and height of the room be l, w, and 2x, respectively. Then we have:
semi-perimeter = (l + w + 2x)/2 = (l + w + 5x)/2
area of walls = 2lw + 2(2x)(l + w) = 2lw + 4xl + 4xw
area of doors and windows = 15
area of walls to be papered = area of walls - area of doors and windows = 2lw + 4xl + 4xw - 15

The area of paper required to paper the walls is equal to the area of walls to be papered multiplied by the width of the paper:
area of paper required = (2lw + 4xl + 4xw - 15)(0.5) = lw + 2xl + 2xw - 7.5

The cost of papering the walls is equal to the area of paper required multiplied by the cost per meter of the paper:
260 = (lw + 2xl + 2xw - 7.5)(2)

Substituting y = 5x, we get:
260 = (lw + 10x^2 - 7.5)(2)
130 = lw + 10x^2 - 7.5
lw + 10x^2 = 137.5

Substituting 5x for y and simplifying, we get:
lw + 50x^2 = 137.5
lw + 5x^2 = 13.75

We know that the area of the room is lw = (semi-perimeter)(height) - 2x(l + w), so we have:
lw = ((l + w + 5x)/2)(2x) - 2x(l + w)
lw = 5x^2

Substituting 5x^2 for lw, we get:
5x^2 + 5x^2 = 13.75
10x^2 = 13.75
x^2 = 1.375
x = sqrt(1.375) = 1.17

Therefore, the height of the room is 2x = 2(1.17) = 2.34m.

Knowledge:
  1. The semi-perimeter of a room is half the sum of the lengths of its four walls.
  2. The cost of papering the room's walls is equal to the cost of papering the area of the walls.
  3. The area of each door and window is subtracted from the total area of the walls to get the area to be papered.
  
Let the height of the room be 2x and the semi-perimeter be 5y. Then we have:
  2y = x(2+5)
  2y = 7x
  y = (7/2)x

Let the length of the longer wall be 2a and the shorter wall be 2b. Then we have:
  5y = a + b + a + b
  5(7/2)x = 2a + 2b
  7x = 2a + 2b

The area of the walls is:
  2x(2a) + 2x(2b) = 4x(a+b)
  
The area of the doors and windows is 15 sq.m, so the area to be papered is:
  4x(a+b) - 15

The cost of papering this area is Rs. 260, so we have:
  260 = 2(0.5)(4x(a+b)-15)
  260 = 4x(a+b) - 15
  4x(a+b) = 275
  2(a+b) = 55x/2
  a+b = 55x/4

Substituting a+b = 55x/4 in the equation 7x = 2a + 2b, we get:
  7x = 2(55x/4)
  x = 4

Therefore, the height of the room is:
  2x = 8 meters

Topic: Math
Question: A man walks at 5 kmph for 6 hrs and at 4 kmph for 12 hrs. His average speed is
Choices:
  A: 4 1/3 km/h
  B: 7 2/3 km/h
  C: 9 ½ km/h
  D: 8 km/h
  E: 81 km/h
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Average speed = Total distance covered / Total time taken
  
Calculation:
  Distance covered in the first 6 hours = 5 kmph * 6 hours = 30 km
  Distance covered in the next 12 hours = 4 kmph * 12 hours = 48 km
  Total distance covered = 30 km + 48 km = 78 km
  Total time taken = 6 hours + 12 hours = 18 hours
  Average speed = 78 km / 18 hours = 4 1/3 km/h
  
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: Average speed is defined as the total distance traveled divided by the total time taken.
  The man walks at 5 kmph for 6 hours, so he covers a distance of 5 x 6 = 30 km.
  He walks at 4 kmph for 12 hours, so he covers a distance of 4 x 12 = 48 km.
  The total distance traveled is 30 + 48 = 78 km.
  The total time taken is 6 + 12 = 18 hours.
Action: Answer("A")  
  The average speed is (total distance traveled) / (total time taken) = 78 / 18 = 4 1/3 km/h.
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  We can use the formula to calculate average speed = Total Distance / Total Time.
  Let us assume the distance traveled at 5 kmph is D1 and distance traveled at 4 kmph is D2.
  We know that Speed = Distance / Time and Time = Distance / Speed.
  Therefore, Distance = Speed * Time.
  Using the above formulas, we can calculate D1 and D2 and then calculate the average speed.
  A: 4 1/3 km/h is not the correct answer.
  B: 7 2/3 km/h is not the correct answer.
  C: 9 ½ km/h is not the correct answer.
  D: 8 km/h is the correct answer.
  E: 81 km/h is not the correct answer.
Action: Answer("D")

  Total time = 6 + 12 = 18 hours.

  Average speed = 4 1/3 km/h

Question: If one third of 3/4 of a number is 21. Then, find the number?
Choices:
  A: 84
  B: 66
  C: 28
  D: 19
  E: 11
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  "One third of" can be represented as 1/3.
  "3/4 of a number" can be represented as 3/4x, where x is the number.
  The equation can be written as (1/3)(3/4x) = 21.
  To solve for x, we need to isolate x by multiplying both sides by (3/4)(3).
  The equation simplifies to x = 84.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
Let's assume that the number is 'x'. 
One third of 3/4 of a number can be written as (1/3)*(3/4)*x which simplifies to (1/4)*x.
Therefore, the equation can be written as (1/4)*x = 21.
To find the value of x, we can multiply both sides by 4. This gives us x = 84.
A: 84 is the correct answer.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  "One third of" means 1/3 multiplied by something.
  "3/4 of a number" means 3/4 multiplied by a number.
  "is" means equals.
  We are looking for a number that satisfies the equation: (1/3) * (3/4) * x = 21, where x is the unknown number.
Action: Answer("B")  
To solve the equation, we can simplify (1/3) * (3/4) to 1/4.
So the equation becomes (1/4) * x = 21.
Multiplying both sides by 4 gives us x = 84.
Therefore, the answer is 84, which corresponds to choice A.

  We know that (1/4)*x = 21.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 46 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The difference between the squares of two numbers is 256000 and the sum of the numbers is 1000. The numbers are
Choices:
  A: 600, 400
  B: 628, 372
  C: 640, 360
  D: None of these
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If x and y are two numbers, then:
  x^2 - y^2 = (x + y)(x - y)
  x + y = sum of two numbers
  We are given that x + y = 1000 and x^2 - y^2 = 256000

Solution:
  x^2 - y^2 = 256000
  (x+y)(x-y) = 256000
  Since x+y = 1000, we have:
  1000(x-y) = 256000
  x-y = 256

  We have two equations:
  x + y = 1000
  x - y = 256

  By adding the two equations, we get:
  2x = 1256
  x = 628

  Substituting x = 628 in x + y = 1000, we get:
  y = 372

  Therefore, the numbers are 628 and 372.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let x and y be the two numbers. Then we have:
  x^2 - y^2 = 256000
  (x+y) = 1000
  We can factor the first equation as (x+y)(x-y) = 256000
  Since (x+y) = 1000, we have x-y = 256 and x+y=1000
  By solving this system of equations, we get x=628 and y=372
Action: Answer("B")

  y = 372

y = 1000 - 628 = 372

Action: Answer("C")
Response 9:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the two numbers are x and y.
  We know that x^2 - y^2 = 256000, which can be factored as (x+y)(x-y) = 256000.
  We also know that x + y = 1000.

Using these equations, we can solve for x and y.

(x+y)(x-y) = 256000
x+y = 1000

Expanding (x+y)(x-y), we get:
x^2 - y^2 = 256000
(x+y)(x-y) = 256000
(x+y)(x-y)/(x+y) = 256000/(x+y)
x-y = 256000/(x+y)

We can now solve for x and y by adding the two equations:

x+y = 1000
x-y = 256000/(x+y)

Adding these two equations, we get:

2x = 1000 + 256000/(x+y)

Multiplying both sides by (x+y), we get:

2x(x+y) = 1000(x+y) + 256000

Expanding and simplifying, we get a quadratic equation:

2x^2 + 2000x - 256000 = 0

Using the quadratic formula, we get:

x = (-2000 ± sqrt(2000^2 + 4(2)(256000))) / (2(2))
x = (-2000 ± 2000) / 4

x = -1000/2 or x = 0

Since the sum of the numbers is 1000, and we can't have a negative number, we can conclude that x = 500.

Now that we know x, we can use x + y = 1000 to solve for y:

y = 1000 - x
y = 1000 - 500
y = 500

Therefore, the two numbers are 500 and 500.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 47 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A company produces 420 units of a particular computer component every month, at a production cost to the company of $110 per component, and sells all of the components by the end of each month. What is the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit (revenue from sales minus production costs) will be at least $626,400 ?
Choices:
  A: 226
  B: 230
  C: 240
  D: 260
  E: 280
Response 0:
Let's start by calculating the yearly production cost of the company:
Yearly production cost = 420 units/month * $110/unit * 12 months/year = $554,400/year

To reach a yearly profit of $626,400, the yearly revenue from sales should be:
Yearly revenue = Yearly production cost + Yearly profit = $554,400/year + $626,400/year = $1,180,800/year

To find the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee the yearly revenue, we can divide the yearly revenue by the number of units produced per year:
Minimum selling price = Yearly revenue / Number of units produced per year = $1,180,800/year / (420 units/month * 12 months/year) = $230/unit

Therefore, the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee the yearly profit will be at least $626,400 is $230.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Let x be the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit will be at least $626,400. 

The revenue from selling one component is x dollars. Thus, the revenue from selling 420 components is 420x dollars. 

The cost of producing one component is $110. Thus, the cost of producing 420 components is 420($110) = $46,200. 

The profit from selling 420 components is the revenue from selling them minus the cost of producing them, which is 420x - $46,200 dollars. 

Since the company wants to make a yearly profit of at least $626,400, the profit from selling 12(420) = 5,040 components (one year's worth) must be at least $626,400. 

So we have the inequality: 

    420x - $46,200 ≥ $626,400/12
    
Simplifying and solving for x: 

    420x - $46,200 ≥ $52,200
    420x ≥ $98,400
    x ≥ $98,400/420
    x ≥ $234.29
    
Rounding up to the nearest dollar, we get x = $235, which is not one of the answer choices. 

The closest answer choice is (B) 230, but that would not be enough to guarantee a yearly profit of at least $626,400. 

Therefore, the answer is None of the Above.
Response 2:
Let's begin by finding the annual revenue from selling all of the components produced each month: 

Annual revenue = Monthly revenue * 12
Monthly revenue = Selling price per unit * Number of units produced - Production cost per unit * Number of units produced
Monthly revenue = (Selling price per unit - Production cost per unit) * Number of units produced
Monthly revenue = (Selling price per unit - $110) * 420
Annual revenue = 420 * 12 * (Selling price per unit - $110)

Next, we can set up an equation to find the minimum selling price that will guarantee the desired yearly profit: 

Profit = Annual revenue - Annual production cost
$626,400 = 420 * 12 * (Selling price per unit - $110) - 420 * 12 * $110

Simplifying and solving for Selling price per unit: 

$626,400 = 420 * 12 * Selling price per unit - 420 * 12 * $110
$626,400 = 5,040 * Selling price per unit - $554,400
$1,180,800 = 5,040 * Selling price per unit
Selling price per unit = $1,180,800 / 5,040
Selling price per unit = $234

Therefore, the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit will be at least $626,400 is $234.

Action: Answer("None of the above")

Calculation:

  420 units/month x $110/unit x 12 months/year = $554,400/year

  $1,180,800/year ÷ 420 units/month ÷ 12 months/year = $230/unit

420 units/month * 12 months/year = 5,040 units/year

Knowledge:
To calculate the minimum selling price, we need to calculate the yearly revenue and yearly production costs first. The yearly revenue is the number of units produced times the selling price per unit. The yearly production costs is the number of units produced times the cost per unit. The yearly profit is the difference between the yearly revenue and the yearly production costs. 

Calculation:
The number of units produced per year is 420*12 = 5040.
Let x be the minimum selling price per component. 
The yearly revenue is 5040*x.
The yearly production costs is 5040*110.
The yearly profit is 5040*x - 5040*110 = 5040*(x-110).
We want the yearly profit to be at least $626,400.
So, we have 5040*(x-110) >= 626400.
Solving for x gives x >= (626400/5040)+110 = 230.

Annual revenue = monthly revenue x 12
Monthly revenue = monthly production x selling price

We know the monthly production is 420 units, so let's find the monthly revenue:
monthly revenue = 420 x selling price

To find the minimum selling price that will guarantee a yearly profit of $626,400, we need to set up an equation for the annual profit as follows:

Annual profit = Annual revenue - Annual production cost
Annual profit = 12 x (monthly revenue) - 12 x (monthly production cost)
Annual profit = 12 x (420 x selling price) - 12 x (420 x $110)
Annual profit = 12 x 420 x (selling price - $110)

$626,400 = 12 x 420 x (selling price - $110)
$626,400 = 5,040 x (selling price - $110)

$6,170,400 = 5,040 x selling price
