Question: A starts travel towards south 3km, then travel 5 km towards east, and again travels 3 km to north, and finally travels 2km towards west. In the end how far from is A from home?
Choices:
  A: 3km
  B: 2km
  C: 4km
  D: 5km
  E: 6km
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  A has traveled 3km to the south, 3km to the north, and 2km to the west. These three distances form a right-angled triangle. We can use the Pythagoras theorem to calculate the hypotenuse of this triangle, which will give us the distance between A's final position and its starting position (home).
  Pythagoras Theorem: c^2 = a^2 + b^2, where c is the hypotenuse and a and b are the other two sides of a right-angled triangle.
Calculation: 
  a = 3km (distance traveled to the south)
  b = 2km (distance traveled to the west)
  c^2 = a^2 + b^2 = 3^2 + 2^2 = 9 + 4 = 13
  c = sqrt(13) (square root of 13)
Action: Answer("E")  
Therefore, A is 6km away from home.

= a2 - 4a2 / 9a2
= -3a2 / 9a2
= -1/3

Therefore, None of these options is correct.

  - To find the time in minutes, we need to divide the distance by the speed and then multiply by 60.

Question: Everyone in the family earns money each month. If the total income of a family per month is $9000 and the median income is $3000, how many members are there in the family?
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 3
  C: 4
  D: 5
  E: 6
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The median is the middle value in a set of numbers when they are arranged in order from least to greatest.
  If the median income is $3000 and there are n members in the family, then the sum of all the incomes can be represented as (n-1)*3000 + (n+1)*3000 = 2n*3000 = 6000n.
  If the total income of the family is $9000, then 6000n = 9000, which implies n = 1.5. Since the number of members in the family must be a whole number, this means that the family cannot have a median income of $3000 with a total income of $9000.
Action: Answer("None of the above")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Median income is the middle income value when a set of incomes are arranged in order from lowest to highest.
  The total income divided by the number of members in the family will give the average income.
Action: Answer("3") 

Explanation:
  If the median income is $3000 and there are n members in the family, then the sum of the n incomes is equal to $9000 because $3000 is the middle value.
  If we assume that the incomes are arranged in order from lowest to highest, then the median income is the income of the (n+1)/2 member.
  Therefore, the income of the (n+1)/2 member is $3000.
  If we add up all the incomes, we get: 
  1st income + 2nd income + ... + (n-1)th income + (n)th income = $9000
  Since the median income is $3000, we can substitute (n+1)/2 as the median income to get:
  1st income + 2nd income + ... + (n-1)th income + (n+1)/2 + (n+3)/2 + ... + nth income = $9000
  Simplifying the equation, we get:
  1st income + 2nd income + ... + (n-1)th income + nth income = $9000
  Since the total income is $9000, the average income is $9000/n.
  Therefore, we can write another equation:
  ($9000/n) = $3000
  Solving for n, we get:
  n = 3
  Therefore, there are 3 members in the family.

  - If the median income is $3000 and there are an equal number of family members earning more and less than $3000, then the sum of the incomes of family members earning more than $3000 must also be $3000.
  - Similarly, the sum of the incomes of family members earning less than $3000 must also be $3000.
  - Therefore, the total number of family members is the sum of the number of family members earning more than $3000 and the number of family members earning less than $3000.
  - Let's assume there are x family members earning more than $3000. Then, there are also x family members earning less than $3000.
  - The total income of family members earning more than $3000 is x * $3000 = $3000x.
  - The total income of family members earning less than $3000 is also x * $3000 = $3000x.
  - The total income of the family is $9000, so $3000x + $3000x = $9000.
  - Simplifying the equation, we get 6x = 9000, which means x = 1500.
  - Therefore, there are x + x = 2x = 2 * 1500 = 3000 / 1000 = 3 family members.
Answer: Answer("B")
Response 8:
Knowledge: 
  The median income is the middle value when a set of incomes is arranged in order from least to greatest.
  If the median income is $3000, then there are an equal number of family members earning less than $3000 and an equal number of family members earning more than $3000.
  If the total income of the family is $9000 and the median income is $3000, then there are three family members earning $3000 each.

Question: A starts a business with Rs.40,000. After 2 months, B joined him with Rs.60,000. C joined them after some more time with Rs.120,000. At the end of the year, out of a total profit of Rs.375,000, C gets Rs.150,000 as his share. How many months after B joined the business, did C join?
Choices:
  A: 2 months
  B: 4 months
  C: 23 months
  D: 24 months
  E: 84 months
Response 0:
Let's start by calculating the share of A and B in the profit. 

Since A invested Rs.40,000 and worked for the entire year, his share of the profit = (40000/220000) x 375000 = Rs. 68,182

B joined after 2 months, so he worked for 10 months. His share of the profit = (60000/220000) x 375000 = Rs. 102,273

Now, we need to find out how long C worked for. Let's assume he worked for x months.

C invested Rs.120,000, so his share of the profit = (120000/220000) x 375000 = Rs. 204,545

We know that C's share of the profit was Rs.150,000, so we can set up an equation:

Rs.150,000 = Rs.204,545 x (x/12)

Solving for x, we get x = 7.27 months.

C joined after B, who worked for 10 months. So, C joined after 10 - 7.27 = 2.73 months. Rounded to the nearest month, C joined after 3 months.

Answer: Option A, 2 months.

x - 2 = 3.875 - 2 = 1.875

Choices:
  A: $50000
  B: $40000
  C: $30000
  D: $20000
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The monthly salary S of a shop assistant is the sum of a fixed salary of $500 plus 5% of all monthly sales.
  We need to find the monthly sales that would make the monthly salary $1500.

Solution:

  Then the monthly salary S can be calculated as follows:
  S = 500 + 0.05x
  We need to find x when S = 1500.
  1500 = 500 + 0.05x
  1000 = 0.05x
  x = 1000/0.05
  x = 20000

Therefore, the monthly sales should be $20000 for the shop assistant to have a monthly salary of $1500.

Question: The sum of k consecutive integers is 51. If the least integer is -50, then k =
Choices:
  A: 40
  B: 62
  C: 82
  D: 92
  E: 102
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If the sum of k consecutive integers starting from n is S, then S = k * n + (k * (k - 1)) / 2.
  Here, the sum of k consecutive integers is given as 51.
  The least integer is given as -50.
  
Solution:
  Let's assume that the k consecutive integers start from x. Then, we can write:
  x + (x+1) + (x+2) + ... + (x+k-1) = 51
  Using the formula for the sum of consecutive integers, we get:
  kx + (k*(k-1))/2 = 51
  We know that the least integer is -50. Therefore, we can write:
  x = -50
  Substituting the values of x and simplifying the equation, we get:
  k^2 + k - 102 = 0
  Factoring the equation, we get:
  (k - 9)(k + 10) = 0
  Since k has to be a positive integer, we can discard the negative root.
  Therefore, k = 9.
  
Answer: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  If the sum of k consecutive integers is 51 and the least integer is -50, then we can use the formula for the sum of an arithmetic series to find k.
  The formula for the sum of an arithmetic series is: S = (n/2)(a1 + an), where S is the sum, n is the number of terms, a1 is the first term, and an is the nth term.
  For this problem, we have S = 51, a1 = -50, and an = a1 + (k-1).
  We can simplify the formula to: S = (n/2)(a1 + a1 + (n-1)d), where d is the common difference.
  Since we are dealing with consecutive integers, the common difference is 1.
  Substituting the values we have, we get: 51 = (k/2)(-50 + (-50 + (k-1)))
  Simplifying the equation, we get: k^2 - 49k - 100 = 0
  Using the quadratic formula, we get: k = (49 +/- sqrt(49^2 + 400))/2 = (49 +/- 51)/2
  Since we are dealing with a positive number of terms, we take the positive root: k = 50/2 = 25

  We can simplify this equation by grouping the integers into pairs with the same absolute value:

  We are also given that the sum of the k consecutive integers is 51.

  If the least integer is -50, then a = -50.
  We are given that the sum is 51.
  Since we don't know the value of k or d, we cannot use the formula directly to solve for k.

  The middle term would be (k+1)/2 terms away from the first term.
  So, the middle term would be -50 + (k+1)/2.
  The sum of the k integers would be k times the middle term, which is k*(-50 + (k+1)/2).

  Multiplying both sides by 2 to get rid of the fraction, we get: 2*k*(-25 + k+1) = 102.

  The sum of an arithmetic sequence is given by S = n/2 * (a_1 + a_n), where n is the number of terms, a_1 is the first term, and a_n is the nth term.
  In this problem, we know the sum of k consecutive integers is 51, and the first term is -50.

  We know that the sum of k consecutive integers is 51, so S = 51.
  We also know that the first term is -50, so a_1 = -50.
  We need to find the value of n, which is the number of terms in the sequence.
  We can use the formula to solve for n:
  S = n/2 * (a_1 + a_n)
  51 = n/2 * (-50 + a_n)
  51 = n/2 * (-50 + (-50 + (n-1)))
  51 = n/2 * (-100 + n - 1)
  51 = n/2 * (n - 101)
  2 * 51 = n^2 - 101n
  n^2 - 101n - 102 = 0
  (n - 102)(n + 1) = 0
  n = 102 or n = -1
  Since we are looking for a positive value of n, we can discard the negative solution.
  Therefore, k = n = 102.

  (12w/x) = (y/t)

  t = xy/(12w)

  t = xy/(720w)

Topic: Math
Question: A rectangular parking space is marked out by painting three of its sides. If the length of the unpainted side is 9 feet, and the sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet, then what is the area of the parking space in square feet?
Choices:
  A: 46
  B: 81
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: None
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The parking space is a rectangle.
  Three of its sides are painted.
  One side is not painted and has a length of 9 feet.
  The sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet.
Action: 
  Let's call the length of the painted sides "L" and the width of the rectangle "W". 
  We know that:
  2L + W = 37  (because there are three sides painted)
  W = 9 (because one side is not painted and has a length of 9 feet)
  We can use these two equations to solve for L:
  2L + 9 = 37
  2L = 28
  L = 14
  Now we can calculate the area of the rectangle:
  A = L * W
  A = 14 * 9
  A = 126
  Therefore, the answer is Choice C: 126.

  l = 9
  Substituting this into the first equation, we get:
  2(9) + w = 37
  18 + w = 37
  w = 19
  So the width of the parking space is 19 feet.

  A = lw = (9)(19) = 171
  Therefore, the area of the parking space is 171 square feet.

Action: 
  Let's assume that the painted sides are length l and width w.
  We know that 2l + w = 37 (sum of the lengths of the painted sides)
  We also know that lw = A (area of the rectangle)
  We can solve for w by rearranging the first equation to get w = 37 - 2l.
  Substituting this into the equation for the area, we get A = l(37 - 2l) = 37l - 2l^2.
  To maximize the area, we can take the derivative of A with respect to l and set it equal to zero.
  dA/dl = 37 - 4l = 0 => l = 37/4 = 9.25.
  Plugging this value of l back into the equation for A, we get A = 9.25(37 - 2(9.25)) = 81.0625.
  Therefore, the area of the parking space is approximately 81 square feet.

  - Let L be the length of the yard in feet.
  - We know that L * 100 = 3,000, since the area of the yard is the product of its length and width.
  - Solving for L, we get L = 3,000 / 100 = 30.

Action: Answer("A")  
The length of the other side of the yard is 30 feet.

Topic: Math
Question: Hoses A and B spout water at different constant rates, and hose A can fill a certain pool in 8 hours. Hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours and the two hoses, working together, then finished filling the pool in another 3 hours. How many hours would it have taken hose B, working alone, to fill the entire pool?
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 15
  C: 12
  D: 6
  E: 3
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  For work problems, we use the formula: 
  1/A + 1/B = 1/T
  where A and B are the individual rates of each hose and T is the time it takes for both hoses working together to fill the pool.
  We can use the formula to find the individual rate of hose A, and then use the individual rate of hose A and the combined rate of both hoses to find the individual rate of hose B.
  
Action: 
  Let's start by finding the individual rate of hose A:
  1/A + 1/B = 1/T
  1/8 + 1/B = 1/(2+3)
  1/8 + 1/B = 1/5
  1/B = 1/5 - 1/8
  1/B = 3/40
  B = 40/3
  The individual rate of hose B is 40/3.
  Now we can use the formula to find how long it would take for hose B to fill the pool alone:
  1/A + 1/B = 1/T
  1/8 + 1/(40/3) = 1/T
  1/8 + 3/40 = 1/T
  5/40 + 3/40 = 1/T
  8/40 = 1/T
  T = 40/8
  T = 5
  Answer: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume the pool has a volume V.
  Hose A can fill the pool alone in 8 hours, so its rate is V/8.
  Hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours, so it filled 2V/8 = V/4 of the pool.
  The two hoses then worked together to fill the remaining 3V/4 of the pool.
  Let's call the rate of Hose B as B.
  When both hoses are working together, their combined rate is V/8 + B = 3V/12 + B = V/4. Therefore, B = V/12.
Action: Answer("B") 

To fill 3/4 of the pool, both hoses together took 3 hours. This means that the rate of both hoses together is 3/4V ÷ 3 = V/4 per hour.
Since Hose A filled 1/4 of the pool in 2 hours, its rate is 1/4 ÷ 2 = 1/8 of the pool per hour.
Let's call the rate of Hose B as B. Then the combined rate of both hoses is V/12 per hour.
We can set up an equation using the rates:
V/4 = 1/8 + V/12
Simplifying this equation, we get:
V/4 - V/12 = 1/8
3V/12 - V/12 = 1/8
2V/12 = 1/8
V = 3/16 of the pool per hour.
So, Hose B can fill the entire pool alone in:
V ÷ (3/16) = (16/3)V hours = 16/3 x 8 hours = 15 hours and 20 minutes.
Rounding to the nearest hour, the answer is 15. Therefore, the answer is (B) 15.
Response 2:
Knowledge:

  Working together, the two hoses can fill the pool in 3 hours, so (3/8)(R_A + R_B)P = P. Thus, we have (3/8)R_A P + (3/8)R_B P = P. Simplifying this equation, we get (3/8)R_A + (3/8)R_B = 1. 
  We want to find the time it takes for hose B to fill the pool alone, which is T_B.
  We know that hose A filled (P/4) of the pool in 2 hours, so R_A = (P/4)/2 = P/8.

Action:

  Now we can use the formula R_A*T_A + R_B*T_B = P and solve for T_B. We know that R_A = P/8, T_A = 2, R_B = 5P/96, and P = 1. Plugging in these values, we get (P/8)*2 + (5P/96)*T_B = 1. Solving for T_B, we get T_B = 12.

  If hose A can fill the pool in 8 hours, then its rate is 1/8 of the pool per hour.

  - In the first 2 hours, hose A filled 2*(1/8) = 1/4 of the pool.
  - In the next 3 hours, hoses A and B together filled (3/8) of the pool.
  - Therefore, hose B filled the remaining (1 - 1/4 - 3/8) = 1/8 of the pool.

  - Solving for x, we get x = 8.

Response 4:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the rate of hose A is "a" and the rate of hose B is "b". 
  We know that the time it takes to fill the pool is 8 hours if only hose A is used.
  We also know that the distance (the pool in this case) is equal to the rate multiplied by the time (d = rt).
  We can use the formula 1/d = 1/a + 1/b to solve the problem.
  
Process:
  Let x be the time it takes for hose B to fill the pool alone. 
  In the first 2 hours, hose A filled 2/8 = 1/4 of the pool.

  1/4a + 1/4b + 3/8a + 3/8b = 1
  Simplifying the equation, we get:
  5/8a + 5/8b = 1
  5/8b = 1 - 5/8a
  b = (8/5)(1 - 5/8a)
  We want to find x, which is the time it takes for hose B to fill the entire pool alone. 
  We can use the formula d = rt to write:
  1 = xa
  1 = xb
  Adding the two equations, we get:
  2 = (a + b)x
  Substituting the expression we found for b, we get:
  2 = (a + (8/5)(1 - 5/8a))x
  Solving for a, we get:
  a = 1/8
  Substituting a = 1/8 into the expression we found for b, we get:
  b = 1/5
  Finally, using the formula d = rt, we can write:
  1 = (1/5)x
  x = 5

Question: Two numbers are in the ratio 3:5. If 9 is subtracted from each, the new numbers are in the ratio 12:23. The smaller number is?
Choices:
  A: 21
  B: 33
  C: 35
  D: 42
  E: 58
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let the two numbers be 3x and 5x, where x is a constant.
  If 9 is subtracted from each, the two numbers become 3x-9 and 5x-9.
  We are told that (3x-9)/(5x-9) = 12/23.
  We need to solve for x and then find the value of 3x, which is the smaller number.
  
Calculation:
  Cross-multiplying the equation (3x-9)/(5x-9) = 12/23, we get:
  23(3x-9) = 12(5x-9)
  Simplifying, we get:
  69x - 207 = 60x - 108
  9x = 99
  x = 11
  Therefore, the smaller number is 3x = 33.
Action: Answer("B")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 65 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If one of the roots of the quadratic equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 is 1.5, then what is the value of m?
Choices:
  A: -23.5
  B: -17.5
  C: -10.5
  D: -16.2
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The sum of the roots of a quadratic equation of the form ax^2 + bx + c = 0 is -b/a, and the product of the roots is c/a.
  If one of the roots of the quadratic equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 is 1.5, then the other root is (-m/1.5).
  The product of the roots is 22, so (1.5)(-m/1.5) = 22, which simplifies to -m = 22/1.5 = 14.67.
Action: Answer("E")  
Explanation: The value of m cannot be determined from the given information.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Quadratic equation: ax^2 + bx + c = 0
  The sum of the roots of a quadratic equation is -b/a
  The product of the roots of a quadratic equation is c/a
  We are given one root, which is 1.5
  
Using the quadratic formula, we can find the other root: 
x = (-b ± sqrt(b^2 - 4ac)) / 2a

In this case, a = 1, b = m, and c = 22, so we have:
1.5 = (-m ± sqrt(m^2 - 4(1)(22))) / 2(1)
3 = -m ± sqrt(m^2 - 88)
3 + m = sqrt(m^2 - 88) or 3 - m = sqrt(m^2 - 88)

Squaring both sides of the equation, we get:
(m + 3)^2 = m^2 - 88 or (m - 3)^2 = m^2 - 88
m^2 + 6m + 9 = m^2 - 88 or m^2 - 6m + 9 = m^2 - 88
6m = 97 or 6m = -97
m = 97/6 or m = -97/6

Since we are looking for the value of m, which is the coefficient of x in the quadratic equation, we choose the solution that is not equal to 1.5:
m = 97/6

Action: Answer("A")

  A quadratic equation has the form ax^2 + bx + c = 0.
  The quadratic formula is x = (-b ± sqrt(b^2 - 4ac)) / 2a.

  If one of the roots of the quadratic equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 is 1.5, then the other root can be found using the product of roots property.
  The sum of the roots of a quadratic equation ax^2 + bx + c = 0 is -b/a.
  Therefore, the sum of the roots of the quadratic equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 is -m.
  So, if one root is 1.5, then the other root is -22/1.5 = -14.67.

Response 3:
Knowledge:
  Quadratic equation is of the form ax^2 + bx + c = 0.
  The sum of the roots of the quadratic equation ax^2 + bx + c = 0 is -b/a.
  The product of the roots of the quadratic equation ax^2 + bx + c = 0 is c/a.

Using the given information:
  Let's assume that the other root of the quadratic equation is r.
  We know that the sum of the roots is -m, so r + 1.5 = -m.
  We also know that the product of the roots is 22, so r * 1.5 = 22.

Solving for r:
  r = 22 / 1.5
  r = 14.67

  r + 1.5 = -m
  14.67 + 1.5 = -m
  16.17 = -m
  m = -16.17

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 66 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In a large forest, 300 deer were caught, tagged, and returned during 2001. During 2002, 500 deer were caught at random, of which only 20 had tags from the previous year. If the percent of deer in the forest that had tags during the second year and were caught in the 500 deer sample is representative of the percent of the total deer population in the forest with tags, what is the total deer population in the forest (assuming no change in population between 2001 and 2002)?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 500
  C: 5000
  D: 6000
  E: 7500
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  We know that 300 deer were tagged in 2001 and returned to the forest, and that the total number of deer caught in 2002 was 500. We also know that 20 of the 500 deer caught in 2002 had tags from the previous year. If we assume that the percentage of tagged deer in the 500 deer sample is the same as the percentage of tagged deer in the total population, then we can set up a proportion to solve for the total population.
Action: 
Let x be the total deer population in the forest. 
The proportion of tagged deer in the 500 deer sample is 20/500 = 0.04 (or 4%). 
The proportion of tagged deer in the total population is 300/x. 
So, we can set up the proportion: 
0.04 = 300/x 
Solving for x: 
x = 300/0.04 = 7500 
Therefore, the total deer population in the forest is 7500. 
Answer: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The number of deer tagged in 2001 is 300.
  The number of deer caught in 2002 is 500.
  The number of deer caught in 2002 with tags from 2001 is 20.
  We assume that the percent of deer with tags caught in the 500 deer sample is representative of the percent of the total deer population in the forest with tags.
  Let x be the total deer population in the forest.

Let's first calculate the percentage of tagged deer in the 500 deer sample:
  The number of tagged deer caught in 2002 is 20.
  Therefore, the percentage of tagged deer in the 500 deer sample is 20/500 = 0.04 = 4%.

  The number of tagged deer in the total population is 0.04x.
  The number of tagged deer in 2001 is 300, so the number of tagged deer in 2002 is also 300.
  Therefore, we have the equation: 300 = 0.04x
  Solving for x, we get x = 7500

Question: In an exam, a candidate secured 504 marks of the maximum mark of M. If the maximum mark M is converted into 800 marks, he would have secured 420 marks. What is the value of M?
Choices:
  A: 278
  B: 2890
  C: 270
  D: 2702
  E: 960
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume the maximum mark M be x.
  In the first scenario, the candidate secured 504 marks out of M.
  In the second scenario, the maximum mark is converted to 800 and the candidate secured 420 marks.
  We can form two equations from the given information.
    First equation: 504/x = y/800  (where y is the marks obtained in the second scenario)
    Second equation: y = 420
  We can solve for x using these equations.
Action: Answer("720") 

Solution:
  Using the first equation, we can find y:
  504/x = y/800
  y = (504 * 800) / x
  y = 403200 / x

  Using the second equation, we know y = 420

  Therefore, we can solve for x:
  420 = 403200 / x
  x = 403200 / 420
  x = 960

  So, the maximum mark M is 960. 
  Answer: E

Question: On dividing 2272 and 875 by a 3-digit number N, we get the same remainder. The sum of the digits of N is:
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 11
  C: 12
  D: 13
  E: 14
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  When two numbers are divided by the same divisor and leave the same remainder, then the difference of the two numbers is divisible by the divisor.
  Let R be the common remainder when 2272 and 875 are divided by N, then
  2272 = pN + R  and 875 = qN + R   for some integers p and q.
  Therefore, 2272 - 875 = (p - q)N, which implies that N divides 1397.
  The 3-digit factors of 1397 are 17 and 82.
  A: The sum of the digits of 17 is 8.
  B: The sum of the digits of 82 is 10.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  When a number is divided by N, the remainder is always less than N.
  If two numbers leave the same remainder when divided by N, then their difference is divisible by N.
  If a number is divisible by 3, then the sum of its digits is also divisible by 3.
  If a number is divisible by 8, then the last three digits of the number are divisible by 8.
  
Calculation:
  Let the 3-digit number be N.
  Let the common remainder be R.
  Then, we can write: 2272 = N x Q + R and 875 = N x P + R, where Q and P are quotients. 
  Subtracting the two equations, we get: 1397 = N x (Q - P).
  Since 1397 is a prime number, its only factors are 1 and itself. Therefore, (Q - P) = 1.
  This means that N divides the difference between the two numbers, which is 1397.
  The prime factors of 1397 are 1397 and 1.
  Therefore, N can be either 1 x 1397 or 1397 x 1.
  However, since N is a 3-digit number, we can eliminate 1 x 1397.
  So, N = 1397.
  The sum of the digits of N is 1 + 3 + 9 + 7 = 20.
  Since 20 is not one of the choices, we need to reduce it further.
  We know that N is divisible by 8, so its last three digits (397) are also divisible by 8.
  The only multiple of 8 that can be obtained by adding one digit to 397 is 400.
  Therefore, the sum of the digits of N is 3 + 9 + 7 + 1 + 4 = 24.

Response 7:
Knowledge: 
  If two numbers p and q leave the same remainder when divided by a number N, then p-q is divisible by N.
  If N is a divisor of a number M, then the remainder obtained when M is divided by N is less than N.
  
Solution:
Let the common remainder be x. Then, we have:
  2272 = aN + x  ...(i)
  875 = bN + x   ...(ii)
  
Subtracting (ii) from (i), we get:
  1397 = (a-b)N
  
This means that N is a divisor of 1397. Now, 1397 is a prime number. Therefore, it has only two divisors: 1 and 1397. 
Hence, N can only be 1 or 1397. If N = 1, then the sum of its digits is 1. However, this will not satisfy the given conditions. 
Therefore, N = 1397 and the sum of its digits is 1+3+9+7 = 20.

Question: By himself, Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours. On a particular day, he happens to finish two-thirds of the work. The remaining portion of the work is done by Jill, whose rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do. How long does it take Jill to finish the remaining work?

  B: 8
  C: 22
  D: 50
  E: 20

  If Jill's rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do, then her rate of cleaning is (5/100) * (1/12) yachts/hour = (1/240) yachts/hour.

  We can use the formula: rate * time = work to solve for "t".
  Jack finished two-thirds of the work, so the remaining one-third of the work is (1/3) yachts.

  Jack's rate of cleaning is (1/12) yachts/hour.
  Jack finished two-thirds of the work, so the remaining one-third of the work is (1/3) yachts.
  ((1/240) * t) = (1/3) - ((1/12) * (2/3))
  ((1/240) * t) = (1/3) - ((1/18))
  ((1/240) * t) = (2/18) - (1/18)
  ((1/240) * t) = (1/18)
  t = (1/18) * (240/1) = 40/3

Topic: Math
Question: Mr.Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to a certain city and return by car. He loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train. How long would he have taken if he had traveled by car in both ways?
Choices:
  A: 22 hrs
  B: 18 hrs
  C: 16 hrs
  D: 20 hrs
  E: 13 hrs
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If Mr. Sam takes x hours to go to the city by train, he also takes x hours to return by car.
  He loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train, which means he saves 4 hours if he goes by car both ways.
  Therefore, the time he takes to go to the city by train and return by car is (2x-4) hours.
  We also know that he takes 17 hours to go by train and return by car.
  Hence, we can form an equation: 2x-4 = 17
  Solving for x, we get x = 10.5
  Therefore, he takes 10.5 hours to go to the city by train and 10.5 hours to return by car.
  So, the total time he takes if he had traveled by car both ways would be 2*10.5 = 21 hours.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume the time it takes Mr. Sam to travel to the city by train be T1 and the time it takes him to return by car be T2. 
  We know that T1 + T2 = 17 and T1-4 = T2 (since he loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train)
  We can rearrange the second equation to get T1 = T2+4.

Working:
  Substituting T2+4 for T1 in the first equation we get:
  (T2+4) + T2 = 17
  Solving for T2 we get: T2 = 6.5

  Since T1 = T2+4, T1 = 10.5

  The total time if he had traveled by car in both ways would be T2+T2 = 2T2 = 13.

Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Let's assume that the time it takes Mr.Sam to go to the city by train is "x" hours. Then, the time it takes him to return by car would also be "x" hours. 

According to the problem, he takes 17 hours to go by train and return by car. So we can write the equation as:

x + x = 17

Simplifying the equation, we get:

2x = 17

x = 8.5

So it takes Mr.Sam 8.5 hours to go to the city by train and 8.5 hours to return by car. 

Now, the problem says that if he goes both ways by train, he loses 4 hours. So, the total time it would take him is:

2x + 4 = 2(8.5) + 4 = 21 hours

Therefore, if he had traveled by car in both ways, he would have taken:

8.5 x 2 = 17 hours

So the answer is A: 22 hrs.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 71 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: For bringing each copper coin from the bottom of a river, a coin-diver gets 20 cents, and for each brass coin she gets 25 cents. If after one dive, she got $3.40. What is the minimum number of copper coins that she brought?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 3
  C: 2
  D: 1
  E: 0
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let's assume that the diver brought x copper coins and y brass coins. 
  For each copper coin, the diver gets 20 cents and for each brass coin, the diver gets 25 cents.
  The total amount of money the diver got after one dive is $3.40.

Calculation:
  We can set up two equations based on the information given:
  1. 20x + 25y = 340 (total amount of money in cents)
  2. x + y = number of coins

  We need to find the minimum number of copper coins, which means we need to minimize the value of x.
  We can use the second equation to solve for y in terms of x: y = number of coins - x

  Substituting this into the first equation, we get:
  20x + 25(number of coins - x) = 340
  20x + 25number of coins - 25x = 340
  5x = 340 - 25number of coins

Topic: Math
Question: The sum of the digits of a three digit number is 17, and the sum of the squares of its digits is 109. If we subtract 495 from the number, we shall get a number consisting of the same digits written in the reverse order. Find the number.
Choices:
  A: 368
  B: 377
  C: 288
  D: 997
  E: 112
Response 0:
Let the three digit number be represented by 'abc'. Then we know that:
a + b + c = 17
a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 109

We can also represent the new number as 'cba' and we know that:
abc - 495 = cba

Solving for a, b, and c using the first two equations, we get:
c = 7
a + b = 10

We can then substitute c = 7 into the second equation to get:
a^2 + b^2 + 49 = 109
a^2 + b^2 = 60

We can now use trial and error to find two numbers that add up to 10 and whose squares add up to 60. These numbers are 4 and 6. Therefore, a = 4 and b = 6.

Substituting a = 4, b = 6, and c = 7 into the equation abc - 495 = cba, we get:
467 - 495 = 764

Therefore, the number is 467.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")  (The answer is not among the choices given)
Response 1:
Let us assume that the three-digit number is 100a + 10b + c. 
Knowledge:
  The sum of the digits of a three-digit number is a + b + c.
  The sum of the squares of the digits of a three-digit number is a^2 + b^2 + c^2.
  If a three-digit number is written in the reverse order, its value is 100c + 10b + a.
We know that:
  a + b + c = 17
  a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 109
  100a + 10b + c - 495 = 100c + 10b + a
Simplifying the third equation:
  99a - 99c = 495
  a - c = 5
  
We can solve for a and c by adding the first and third equations:
  2a + b = 22
Solving the above equation for b in terms of a, we get:
  b = 22 - 2a
  
Substituting the values of a and b in the third equation, we get:
  100a + 10b + c - 495 = 100c + 10b + a
  99a - 99c = 495
  a - c = 5
Solving the above two equations, we get:
  a = 8
  b = 3
  c = 4
  
Therefore, the three-digit number is 834, and the answer is A: 368.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 73 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Fernando purchased a university meal plan that allows him to have a total of 3 lunches and 3 dinners per week. If the cafeteria is closed on weekends and Fernando always goes home for a dinner on Friday nights, how many options does he have to allocate his meals?
Choices:
  A: 5C3*4C3
  B: 5C4*4C2
  C: 5C2*4C4
  D: 5C6*4C5
  E: 4C3*4C3
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Fernando has 3 lunch options and 3 dinner options per week.
  Fernando goes home for dinner on Friday nights, so he only needs to allocate 2 dinners per week.
  The number of ways to choose k items from a set of n distinct items is given by the binomial coefficient C(n,k), which is equal to n!/[(n-k)!k!].

Analysis:
  Fernando has 3 lunch options and 2 dinner options to allocate for the weekdays.
  He can choose 3 lunches from 3 options in C(3,3) = 1 way.
  He can choose 2 dinners from 2 options in C(2,2) = 1 way.
  Therefore, he has 1 way to allocate his meals on weekdays.
  The total number of options is the product of the number of options for weekdays and weekends.
  He has 1 option for weekdays and 1 option for weekends.

  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the length of a diagonal of the cube.
  If the side of the cube is s, then the diameter of the sphere is s√3.
  Therefore, the radius of the sphere is (s/2)√3.
  The ratio of the volumes of the cube to the sphere is s^3 / [(4/3)π(s/2)^3(3)] = (6/π).

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 76 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm?
Choices:
  A: 50
  B: 70
  C: 75
  D: 100
  E: 125
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let's use the following variables:
  - v: the number of files infected by a virus
  - w: the number of files infected by a worm
  - b: the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm
  We know that:
  - v + w - b = 250 (since all files are either infected by a virus, a worm, or both)
  - w - 2.5b = 0.4(250) (since the number of files infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm, and 50% of the files were not infected by a virus)
Action: 
  We can solve the system of equations:
  v + w - b = 250
  0v + w - 2.5b = 100
  Multiplying the second equation by 2 and adding it to the first equation, we get:
  v + 4w = 450
  Since we know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, we have:
  v = 0.5(250) = 125
  Substituting v = 125 in v + 4w = 450, we get:
  125 + 4w = 450
  4w = 325
  w = 81.25
  Substituting v = 125 and w = 81.25 in v + w - b = 250, we get:
  125 + 81.25 - b = 250
  b = 43.75
  The number of files that were not infected by a worm is:
  125 + b = 125 + 43.75 = 168.75
  Since we can't have a fraction of a file, the closest answer is C: 75. Therefore, the answer is Answer("C").
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
Let V be the number of files infected only by a virus, 
W be the number of files infected only by a worm, and 
VW be the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm. 
We know that V + W + VW = 250 and W = 2.5 * VW. 
We also know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus.

Action: 
If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, then the total number of files infected by a virus is 0.5 * 250 = 125.
Therefore, V + VW = 125. 
Substituting W = 2.5 * VW into the equation above, we get V + 3.5 * VW = 125.
Substituting VW = (250 - W - V) / 2.5 into the equation above, we get V + 3.5 * [(250 - W - V) / 2.5] = 125.
Simplifying the equation above, we get 7V + 5W = 875.

We want to find the number of files that were NOT infected by a worm, which is equal to the number of files that were either not infected by anything or infected only by a virus. 
We know that V + W + VW = 250 and V + VW = 125, so W = 250 - V - VW = 250 - V - 0.5V = 250 - 1.5V.
We want to find 125 - W - V, which is equal to 125 - (250 - 1.5V) - V = 375 - 2.5V.

To find V, we can solve the system of equations:
7V + 5W = 875
W = 2.5 * VW
V + W + VW = 250

Substituting W = 2.5 * VW and VW = (W + V - 250)/(-1) into the first equation, we get:
7V + 5(2.5 * VW) = 875
7V + 12.5V - 31.25 = 875
19.5V = 906.25
V = 46.538

Substituting V = 46.538 and W = 250 - V - VW into the second equation, we get:
46.538 + (250 - 46.538 - VW) + VW = 250
VW = 46.538

Substituting V = 46.538 and VW = 46.538 into the third equation, we get:
46.538 + W + 46.538 = 250
W = 157.924

Therefore, the number of files that were NOT infected by a worm is 375 - 2.5V = 375 - 2.5(46.538) = 260.655, which is closest to 260.655 ≈ 260.

Knowledge: 
Let V be the number of files infected by a virus only, 
W be the number of files infected by a worm only, and

1. V + W + B = 250   (all files are either infected by a virus or a worm or both)

3. V = 0.5(250) = 125 (50% of files were not infected by a virus)

Topic: Math
Question: A trader sold an article at a profit of 20% for Rs.360. What is the cost price of the article?
Choices:
  A: 270
  B: 300
  C: 280
  D: 320
  E: 315
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price
  Profit% = (Profit/Cost Price) * 100
  A: Cost Price = Selling Price - Profit
  B, C, D, E: These options need to be calculated.

Calculation:
  Let's assume the cost price of the article is x.
  Profit = 20% of x = (20/100)*x = 0.2x
  Selling Price = Cost Price + Profit = x + 0.2x = 1.2x
  It is given that Selling Price = Rs.360
  Therefore, 1.2x = 360
  Solving for x, we get x = 300

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Profit percentage = (Profit/Cost Price) × 100
  Selling Price = Cost Price + Profit

Calculation:

Profit percentage = 20%
Profit = (20/100) × x = 0.2x
Selling Price = Cost Price + Profit = x + 0.2x = 1.2x
Given, Selling Price = Rs.360
1.2x = 360
x = 300

where Profit (P) = 20% of Cost Price (CP) = 0.2CP

Given, 
SP = Rs. 360
P = 20% of CP = 0.2CP

Calculation:
Substituting the given values in the formula,
SP = CP + P
360 = CP + 0.2CP
360 = 1.2CP
CP = 360/1.2
CP = 300

Question: A newspaper costs $4 on Sunday and $1 the rest of the days of the week. If a hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week and pays $210 per week for newspapers, how many newspapers does it buy on Monday?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 30
  C: 45
  D: 60
  E: 75
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let's call the number of newspapers bought on Sunday "s" and the number of newspapers bought on the other days of the week "d". 
  We know that s = 2d. 
  We also know that the hotel pays $4 for each Sunday paper and $1 for each paper bought on the other days of the week.
  We can set up an equation to represent the total cost per week: 4s + 1(6d) = 210, which simplifies to 4s + 6d = 210.

Action: 
  Let's use the fact that s = 2d and solve for d:
  4s + 6d = 210
  4(2d) + 6d = 210
  8d + 6d = 210
  14d = 210
  d = 15
  So the hotel buys 15 newspapers on Monday.
  Answer: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Let's start by using algebra to represent the problem. 

Let x be the number of newspapers bought on Monday. 
Then the number of newspapers bought on Sunday is 2x. 
The number of newspapers bought from Monday to Saturday is 6x. 

We know that the hotel pays $4 for each Sunday newspaper and $1 for each newspaper bought on the other days. So the total cost per week is:

4(2x) + 1(6x) = 8x + 6x = 14x

We also know that the hotel pays $210 per week for newspapers:

14x = 210

Solving for x, we get:

x = 15

Therefore, the hotel buys 15 newspapers on Monday.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Let's assume that the hotel buys X newspapers on each day of the week except Sunday. Then, it buys 2X newspapers on Sunday. 

The cost of X newspapers on each day of the week except Sunday is $1 per newspaper, so the cost of X newspapers for the six days is $6X. 

The cost of 2X newspapers on Sunday is $4 per newspaper, so the cost of 2X newspapers on Sunday is $8X. 

The total cost of newspapers for the week is $210, so we have:

$6X + $8X = $210

Simplifying this equation, we get:

$14X = $210

X = $210 / $14

X = 15

Therefore, the hotel buys 15 newspapers on each of the six days of the week, which is a total of 90 newspapers for the week. 

The hotel buys twice as many newspapers on Sunday, so it buys 30 newspapers on Sunday. 

Therefore, the hotel buys a total of 120 newspapers per week, and it buys 15 newspapers on Monday.

  B: 30
  C: 6
  D: 15
  E: 12
Response 0:

  The reduction ratio is 5:3, which means that the original length was divided by 5+3=8 parts, and the reduced length is 3 parts.
  To find the reduced length, we can multiply the original length by the fraction representing the reduced ratio: 3/5.
Action: Answer("18")

  The length of ribbon was reduced by 5 out of those 8 parts.

  Therefore, the length of the ribbon now is 19 cm.

  - Let the original length of the ribbon be x. 
  - The new length of the ribbon is (5-3)/5 times x = 2/5 times x.
  - Therefore, the new length of the ribbon is 2/5 times 30 cm = 12 cm.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The distance between X and Y is the same for both Allen and Bob.
  - When they meet for the second time, they would have traveled the same distance.
  - The distance traveled by Allen and Bob from X and Y respectively is the same.
  - To solve the problem, we need to use the formula: distance = speed × time.
  
Solution:
  Let's assume that the distance between X and Y is d km.
  Let's also assume that they meet for the second time after t hours.
  
  In the first part of the journey, Allen travels from X to Y, a distance of d km, at a speed of 54 kmph.
  Therefore, the time taken by Allen to travel from X to Y is given by:
  time = distance / speed = d / 54
  
  In the same time, Bob travels from Y to X, a distance of d km, at a speed of 78 kmph.
  Therefore, the distance covered by Bob in the same time is given by:
  distance = speed × time = 78 × (d / 54) = (13/9) d
  
  When they meet for the first time, the total distance covered by both of them is d km.
  Therefore, the distance covered by Allen in the first part of the journey is:
  d - (13/9) d = (8/9) d
  
  In the second part of the journey, Allen travels from Y to X, a distance of d km, at a speed of 54 kmph.
  Therefore, the time taken by Allen to travel from Y to X is given by:
  time = distance / speed = d / 54
  
  In the same time, Bob travels from X to Y, a distance of d km, at a speed of 78 kmph.
  Therefore, the distance covered by Bob in the same time is given by:
  distance = speed × time = 78 × (d / 54) = (13/9) d
  
  When they meet for the second time, the total distance covered by both of them is 2d km.
  Therefore, the distance covered by Allen in the second part of the journey is:
  d - (13/9) d = (8/9) d
  
  We know that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen in the same time.
  Therefore, (13/9) d - d = 48
  Solving for d, we get d = 144.
  
  Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 144 km.
  
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:

  - Allen and Bob start at opposite points and travel towards each other until they meet.

d - 48 = 132t2

d - 48 = 132t2

d - 48 = 2d(31/39)
39d - 1872 = 62d
23d = 1872
d = 81.39

Response 3:
Knowledge:
  - We can use the formula Distance = Speed x Time (D = S x T) to solve this problem.
  - When Allen and Bob meet for the first time, they have both traveled the same distance.
  - Let's call the distance between X and Y "D". 
  - Let's call the distance that Allen traveled from X to Y "d". Therefore, he traveled "D - d" in the opposite direction towards X.
  - Let's call the time it takes for Allen to travel from X to Y "t" and the time it takes for Bob to travel from Y to X "T". 

Solution:
  - We know that distance = speed x time. Therefore, time = distance / speed.
  - The time it takes for Allen to travel from X to Y is t = d / 54.
  - The time it takes for Bob to travel from Y to X is T = (D - d) / 78.
  - When they meet for the first time, they have both traveled the same distance. Therefore:
    d + 78T = (D - d) + 54t
    d + 78(D - d) / 78 = (D - d) + 54d / 54
    d + D - d = D - d + 54d / 54 - 78D / 78 + 78d / 78
    D = 132d / 78
  - When they meet for the second time, Allen has traveled a total of D, and Bob has traveled a total of D + 48.
  - The time it takes for Allen to travel from Y to X is T = (D - d) / 54.
  - The time it takes for Bob to travel from X to Y is t = d / 78.
  - When they meet for the second time, they have both traveled a total distance of D + D - d = 2D - d.
    Therefore, we can write the following equation:
    54T + 78t = 2D - d
    54(D - d) / 54 + 78d / 78 = 2D - d
    D - d + d = 2D - d
    D = 2D - d
    D = d

  - We can substitute D = 132d / 78 into the equation above:
    132d / 78 = d
    d = 72
  - Therefore, the distance between X and Y is D = 132d / 78 = 132 x 72 / 78 = 122 km.

  - The time taken for both of them to reach the second meeting point is the same, so we can use the formula: time = distance / speed.
  - Therefore, (2d-x) / 54 = (2x+d+48) / 78.

Distance traveled by Bob = Speed x Time = 78t2

Speed = 78 kmph
Time taken to return to Y = t3
Distance traveled by Bob = Speed x Time = 78t3

Total distance traveled by Bob = 78t2 + 78t3

We know that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen by the second meeting. This means that the total distance traveled by Bob is equal to the total distance traveled by Allen plus 48 km.

78t2 + 78t3 = 54t1 + 54t3 + 48

We also know that they meet twice, once at Y and once at X, so the total time taken by both of them is the same.

t1 + t2 = t3

We can use this equation to eliminate t2 in terms of t1 and t3:

t2 = t3 - t1

Now we can substitute this into the equation we derived earlier:

3t3 - 3t1 = 1/4

t1 = 7/3

7/3 + t2 = 2t1

7/3 + t2 = 14/3

t2 = 7/3

Distance traveled by Bob = 78t2 + 78t3 = 78(7/3) + 78(8/9) = 222 km

Total distance traveled by both of them = 154 + 222 = 376 km

Distance between X and Y = Total distance traveled by both of them / 2 = 376 / 2 = 188 km

Knowledge:
  When two objects start moving towards each other, the relative speed of the objects is the sum of their individual speeds.
  When two objects start moving towards each other, the time it takes to meet is the distance between them divided by the relative speed.
  The distance traveled by an object is the product of the speed and time.
  
Let the distance between X and Y be d.
Let the time for Allen to reach Y be t.
The relative speed of Allen and Bob is 54 + 78 = 132 kmph.
The distance traveled by Allen before he reaches Y is 54t.
The distance traveled by Bob before they meet for the first time is 78t.
The distance between them at this point is d - 78t.
The time it takes for them to meet for the first time is (d - 78t)/132.
The distance traveled by Bob before they meet for the second time is 2 * 78 * (d - 78t)/132 = 2 * 13/22 * (d - 78t).
The distance traveled by Allen before they meet for the second time is 2 * 54t = 108t.

2 * 13/22 * (d - 78t) - 108t = 48

13/11 * d - 936/11 = 108t + 48

13/11 * d - 936/11 = 9/11 * (2d - 134t)
13d - 936 = 198d/11 - 1206t
1206t = 198d/11 - 13d + 936
t = (198d/11 - 13d + 936)/1206

d = 144

Question: A jeep travels a certain distance taking 6 hours in the forward journey. During the return journey, it increased its speed by 12km/hr and took 4 hours. What is the distance travelled by the jeep?
Choices:
  A: 126km
  B: 144km
  C: 127km
  D: 228km
  E: 128km
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let's assume the speed of the jeep on the forward journey is x km/hr.
  The speed of the jeep on the return journey is x + 12 km/hr.
  Using the formula distance = speed x time, we can calculate the distance travelled by the jeep.
  On the forward journey, the distance travelled is x * 6.
  On the return journey, the distance travelled is (x + 12) * 4.
  We can use these two equations to solve for the distance travelled by the jeep.
  
Calculation:
  Distance travelled on forward journey = x * 6
  Distance travelled on return journey = (x + 12) * 4
  Total distance travelled = Distance travelled on forward journey + Distance travelled on return journey
  Total distance travelled = x * 6 + (x + 12) * 4
  Total distance travelled = 6x + 4x + 48
  Total distance travelled = 10x + 48
  
We need to find the value of Total distance travelled. We need to find the value of x to calculate the Total distance travelled.

Calculation continued:
  We know that the jeep travelled the same distance in both the forward and return journey.
  Therefore, distance travelled on forward journey = Distance travelled on return journey
  x * 6 = (x + 12) * 4
  6x = 4x + 48
  2x = 48
  x = 24
  
  Now, we can calculate the Total distance travelled.
  Total distance travelled = 10x + 48
  Total distance travelled = 10 * 24 + 48
  Total distance travelled = 240 + 48
  Total distance travelled = 288

Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The number of water lilies doubles every two days.
  It took 60 days for the lake to be fully covered when there was only one water lily initially.
  If initially there were 64 water lilies, we need to find how many days it takes for the lake to be fully covered.
  
Solution:
  If the number of water lilies doubles every two days, then if there are n water lilies on the lake, there were n/2 water lilies two days ago.
  If initially there were 64 water lilies, then 2 days ago there were 32 water lilies.
  4 days ago there were 16 water lilies, 6 days ago there were 8 water lilies, and so on.
  We can write this in a formula: n/64 = 2^(t/2), where n is the number of water lilies and t is the number of days.
  If n is the number of water lilies we need to fully cover the lake, then n = 2^k, where k is the number of doublings needed to get from 64 to n.
  We can substitute n = 2^k into the formula above and get 2^k/64 = 2^(t/2), which simplifies to k = 6 + t/2.
  If we substitute n = 2^6 = 64 into the formula above, we get k = 6, which means it takes 6 doublings to get from 64 to 2^12 = 4096 water lilies.
  Therefore, 6 + t/2 = 60, which implies t/2 = 54 and t = 108.
  The lake will be fully covered with lilies in 108 days.
Answer: Answer("E")

Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another?
Choices:
  A: 1 hr 23 min
  B: 1 hr 15 min
  C: 1 hr 8 min
  D: 56 min
  E: 55 min
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9 am, so it takes 4 hours to travel from A to B.
  Train N leaves City B at 7 am and reaches City A at 10:30 am, so it takes 3.5 hours to travel from B to A.
  The trains are traveling towards each other.
  The distance between City A and City B is the same for both trains.
Action: Answer("E")  
  Let's find the time interval between when Train N leaves and when the trains meet.
  Train N leaves City B at 7 am, and Train M has already been traveling for 2 hours (since 5 am).
  Therefore, the time interval between when Train N leaves and when the trains meet is 2 hours and 30 minutes (from 7 am to 9:30 am).
  Since the trains are getting closer at a combined rate of (M + N), and the distance between them is constant, we can use the formula: distance = rate * time.
  Let's assume that the distance between City A and City B is d.
  Then, the rate of Train M is d/4 (distance divided by time), and the rate of Train N is d/3.5.
  The combined rate of the trains is (d/4) + (d/3.5) = (8.5d/35) + (10d/35) = (18.5d/35).
  We want to find the time it takes for the trains to meet, so we can rearrange the formula to get: time = distance / rate.
  Plugging in the values, we get: time = d / (18.5d/35) = 35/18.5 hours = 1.89 hours.
  Converting to minutes, we get 1 hour and 53.4 minutes. 
  So, the trains will meet 1 hour and 53.4 minutes after Train N leaves, which is at 8:53.4 am.
  To find the time interval between when Train M leaves and when the trains meet, we subtract 2 hours (the time Train M has been traveling before Train N leaves) from 8:53.4, which gives us 6:53.4 am.
  The time interval between when Train M leaves and when the trains meet is therefore 55.4 minutes, which is closest to choice E: 55 min.

Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?
Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The formula for the mean is: mean = sum of all values / number of values.
  Let's call the sum of the weights of the first 10 vehicles "S" and the weight of the new truck "x". 
  Then, from the given information, we have:
  mean = (S + x) / 11
  mean - 2.6 = S / 10
  Solving for S in the second equation, we get:
  S = 10(mean - 2.6)
  Substituting this into the first equation, we get:
  mean = (10(mean - 2.6) + x) / 11
  Solving for x, we get:
  x = 41.6

    We need to find x, which is the weight of the new heavy duty truck, so we can solve for x:
    - S1 + x = S2
    - x = S2 - S1
    We can substitute S1 and S2 in the equation above:
    - x = (14.8 * 11) - (12.2 * 10)
    - x = 40.6

  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:

Solving for x:

x = 20/7

Response 1:

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 88 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The perimeter of a rectangle can be calculated by adding all four sides of the rectangle.
  The perimeter of a rectangle can also be calculated as 2 times the length plus 2 times the width.
  We are given the perimeter of a rectangular plot. 
  We need to find the dimensions of the rectangular plot to calculate the area.
  Once we have the area, we can multiply it by the rate of 10 per square meter to find the cost.
Action: 
  Let L be the length of the rectangular plot and W be the width.
  We are given that 2L + 2W = 340.
  Dividing both sides by 2, we get L + W = 170.
  We need to find the area of the rectangular plot, which is L x W.
  We can solve for one variable in terms of the other using L = 170 - W.
  Substituting into the area formula, we get A = (170 - W)W.
  Expanding and simplifying, we get A = 170W - W^2.
  This is a quadratic function, with a maximum value at the axis of symmetry.
  The axis of symmetry is W = -b/2a = -170/-2 = 85.
  Therefore, the maximum area occurs when W = 85.
  Plugging in W = 85, we get L = 170 - W = 85.
  Therefore, the dimensions of the rectangular plot are 85 meters by 85 meters.
  The area of the rectangular plot is 85 x 85 = 7225 square meters.
  The cost of gardening 1-meter boundary around the rectangular plot at the rate of 10 per square meter is 7225 x 10 = 72250.
  Answer: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The perimeter of a rectangle is the sum of all its sides.
  If the length of a rectangle is L and its width is W, then its perimeter is 2(L+W).
  The given perimeter of the rectangular plot is 340 meters.
  Let the length of the rectangular plot be L and its width be W.
  The length of the plot will be (340-2W)/2 since the perimeter is 2(L+W).
  The width of the plot will be (340-2L)/2.
  The area of the rectangular plot will be L*W.
  The cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary around the plot will be the cost of gardening an area equal to (L+2)(W+2) minus the cost of gardening an area equal to L*W. This cost will be (L+2)(W+2) - L*W multiplied by 10.

Calculations:
  (340-2W)/2 + (340-2L)/2 = L + W
  340 - W - L = L + W
  2W = 340 - 2L
  W = 170 - L
  L*W = L(170-L) = -L^2 + 170L
  (L+2)(W+2) = (L+2)(172-L) = -L^2 + 168L + 344
  (L+2)(W+2) - L*W = 168L + 344
  Cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary = (168L + 344)*10 = 1680L + 3440

Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Perimeter of a rectangle = 2(length + width)
  Cost of gardening = area of the garden * rate
  Area of the garden = (length + 2 * boundary) * (width + 2 * boundary) - length * width, where boundary is 1 meter
  
Calculation:
  Let L be the length and W be the width of the rectangle.
  Perimeter = 2(L + W) = 340 meters
  L + W = 170 meters
  Area of the garden = (L + 2) * (W + 2) - L * W = LW + 2L + 2W + 4 - L * W = 2L + 2W + 4
  Cost of gardening = Area of the garden * rate = (2L + 2W + 4) * 10 = 20L + 20W + 40
  
  We know L + W = 170, so we can substitute W = 170 - L into the equation above to get:
  Cost of gardening = 20L + 20(170 - L) + 40 = 20L + 3400
  
Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  Perimeter of a rectangle = 2(length + width)
  The given perimeter of the rectangular plot is 340 meters, so 2(length + width) = 340 meters.
  We are given the rate of 10 per square metre for gardening.
  The rectangular plot has a 1-meter broad boundary around it.
  We need to calculate the area of the rectangular plot along with the area of the 1-meter broad boundary.
  To calculate the area of a rectangle, we use the formula A = length × width.
  To calculate the area of the 1-meter broad boundary, we need to add the area of the four sides (since each side has a width of 1 meter).
  A = (length + 2) × (width + 2) - length × width
  
Calculations:
  Let's first calculate the length and width of the rectangular plot using the given perimeter.
  2(length + width) = 340
  length + width = 170
  We are not given the length and width of the rectangular plot, but we know that their sum is 170.
  Let's assume the length of the plot to be 85 meters and the width to be 85 meters as well.
  Now let's calculate the area of the rectangular plot along with the area of the 1-meter broad boundary.
  A = (length + 2) × (width + 2) - length × width
  A = (85 + 2) × (85 + 2) - 85 × 85
  A = 9241 square meters
  Now let's calculate the cost of gardening.
  Cost = Area × Rate
  Cost = 9241 × 10
  Cost = 92410

  We are given the perimeter of the rectangular plot, which is 340 meters.

  We need to find the cost of gardening a 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot.

Solution:
  Let the length and breadth of the rectangular plot be l and b, respectively.
  Perimeter of the rectangular plot = 2(l+b) = 340 meters
  l + b = 170 meters
  Length of the rectangular plot including the 1-meter broad boundary = l + 2(1) + l = 2l + 2 meters
  Breadth of the rectangular plot including the 1-meter broad boundary = b + 2(1) + b = 2b + 2 meters
  Area of the 1-meter broad boundary = (2l + 2) x 1 + (2b + 2) x 1 = 2l + 2b + 4 square meters
  Cost of gardening 1 square meter is given as 10.
  Cost of gardening the 1-meter broad boundary = 10 x (2l + 2b + 4) = 20l + 20b + 40

Answer: Answer("C")  (3440)

Question: Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
Choices:
  A: 50 %
  B: 60 %
  C: 55 %
  D: 70 %
  E: 58%

Knowledge:
  Percentage gain is calculated using the formula: (Profit/Cost Price) x 100%
  Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price
  
Calculation:
  Cost price of 90 kg of oranges = Rs. 450
  Cost price per kg = 450/90 = Rs. 5
  Selling price per kg = Rs. 7.50
  Selling price of 90 kg of oranges = 7.50 x 90 = Rs. 675
  Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price = 675 - 450 = Rs. 225
  Percentage gain = (Profit/Cost Price) x 100% = (225/450) x 100% = 50%

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Let's assume that Joe's age is "J", his sister's age is "S", and his father's age is "F". 

From the first sentence, we know that: J + S + F = 100. 

From the second sentence, we know that when J = F, S + (J - F) = 2S. Simplifying this equation gives us J - F = S. 

From the third sentence, we know that when J = F, F = 2(S - F). Simplifying this equation gives us F = 2S/3. 

Now we can solve for the variables. 

Substituting F = 2S/3 into the first equation gives us: J + S + 2S/3 = 100. Simplifying this equation gives us: J = 100 - 5S/3. 

Substituting J - F = S into F = 2S/3 gives us: J - F = S = S/3. Simplifying this equation gives us: J = 4S/3. 

Substituting J = 4S/3 into J = 100 - 5S/3 gives us: 4S/3 = 100 - 5S/3. Simplifying this equation gives us: S = 27. 

Substituting S = 27 into F = 2S/3 gives us: F = 18. 

Therefore, the age of Joe's father is 18. 

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Let's assume that Joe's age is "J", his sister's age is "S", and his father's age is "F". 

From the first condition, we can write an equation: 

J + S + F = 100  (Equation 1)

From the second condition, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. If we assume that x years later, Joe will be as old as his father, then we can write: 

S + x = 2(S)  (Equation 2)

Solving Equation 2 for x, we get: 

x = S 

This means that when Joe is as old as his father, his sister's age will be S + S = 2S, which is twice her current age. 

From the third condition, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, his father will be twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. If we assume that y years ago, Joe's sister was as old as her father, then we can write: 

S - y = F 

Solving Equation 3 for y, we get: 

y = S - F 

This means that when Joe is as old as his father, his father's age will be F + x, and his sister's age will be S + x. Substituting the values of x and y, we get: 

F + S = 2(S - (S - F))
F + S = 2F
S = F 

Substituting S = F in Equation 1, we get: 

J + 2F = 100

Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Each time the coin lands on heads, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan.
  Each time the coin lands on tails, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher.
  After 20 flips, no one has won or lost any money.
  
Solution:
  Let x be the number of times the coin landed on heads.
  Then, the number of times the coin landed on tails is 20 - x.
  The amount of money Christopher gives to Jonathan is 2x.
  The amount of money Jonathan gives to Christopher is 3(20 - x) = 60 - 3x.
  Since no one has won or lost any money, we have 2x = 60 - 3x.
  Solving for x, we get x = 12.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  If the coin lands on Heads, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan. 
  If the coin lands on Tails, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher.
  After flipping the coin for twenty times, none of them won or lost any amount.
  This means that the amount Christopher gave to Jonathan is equal to the amount Jonathan gave to Christopher.
  The difference between the amount Christopher gave to Jonathan and the amount Jonathan gave to Christopher is always a multiple of 5.
  If x is the number of times the coin landed on Heads, then (20-x) is the number of times the coin landed on Tails. 
  The money Christopher gave to Jonathan is 2x, and the money Jonathan gave to Christopher is 3(20-x) = 60-3x.
  Therefore, 2x = 60 - 3x, which implies 5x = 60, and x = 12.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 95 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph.
  Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph.
  Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it.
  Let's assume the distance between A and B is "d".
  Let's assume the time it took Kevin to get to B is "t".
  The time it took Kevin to return to A is also "t".
  We know that: distance = rate x time.
Action: 
  Let's start by finding out how long it took Kevin to reach B:
  distance = rate x time
  d = 70t
  Let's find out how long it took Kevin to return to A:
  distance = rate x time
  d = 90t
  We know that 3 hours before the end of his trip he was 70 miles away from B.
  This means that he had already traveled d-70 miles towards A.
  Let's calculate how long it took him to travel d-70 miles:
  distance = rate x time
  d-70 = 90(t-3)
  d-70 = 90t - 270
  d = 90t - 200
  We can substitute the first two equations into the third equation:
  d = 70t + 90t - 200
  d = 160t - 200
  We can substitute this equation into the first equation:
  d = 70t
  160t - 200 = 70t
  90t = 200
  t = 2.22
  Now we can substitute t into any of the previous equations to get d:
  d = 70t
  d = 70 x 2.22
  d = 155.4
  The distance between A and B is approximately 155.4 miles.
  Answer: Answer("E") None of the above. The correct answer is approximately 155.4 miles.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - Distance = Rate * Time
  - If d is the distance between A and B and t1 is the time it takes Kevin to drive from A to B, then:
    - d = 70 * t1 (since he drove at 70 mph)
    - d = 90 * (t1 + t2) (since he drove at 90 mph on the way back, where t2 is the time it takes him to return to A)
    - 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was 70 miles away from B, so he had 70 miles left to travel and (t1 + t2 - 3) hours to complete the trip.
  - We can use these equations to solve for d.
  
Solution:
  - From the first equation, we get t1 = d/70.
  - Substituting t1 into the second equation, we get d = 90 * ((d/70) + t2).
  - Simplifying this equation, we get d = (900/7) * t2.
  - Substituting d into the third equation, we get (900/7) * t2 = 70 + 90 * (t1 + t2 - 3).
  - Substituting t1 = d/70 = (900/7) * t2 / 70 into the equation above, we get:
    (900/7) * t2 = 70 + 90 * ((900/7) * t2 / 70 + t2 - 3)
    Simplifying this equation, we get t2 = 4.
  - Substituting t2 = 4 into the equation for d, we get d = 360.

  - We can solve for t1 and t2 by substituting d in the second equation with 70t1 from the first equation:
    - 70t1 - 70 = 90t2
    - 7t1 - 9t2 = 7
  - We also know that t1 + t2 = total time of the trip, so we can substitute t2 with t - t1:
    - 7t1 - 9(t - t1) = 7
    - 16t1 - 9t = 7
    - 16t1 - 9(t1 + t2) = 7
    - 16t1 - 9t1 - 9t2 = 7
    - 7t1 - 9t2 = 7
    - We get the same equation as before, which means that t1 = 16/7 and t2 = 23/7
  - Finally, we can substitute t1 into one of the equations we created earlier to find d:
    - d = 70t1
    - d = 70 x 16/7
    - d = 160

Response 8:
Knowledge:
  - Distance = Speed x Time
  - Time = Distance / Speed
  
Let's call the distance between A and B "d". 
Let's call the time it takes for Kevin to travel from A to B "t".
Let's call the time it takes for Kevin to travel from B to A "u".

We know that Kevin traveled at a constant speed of 70 mph from A to B, so:

  t = d / 70

We also know that Kevin traveled at a constant speed of 90 mph from B to A, so:

  u = d / 90

We know that Kevin was 70 miles away from B, 3 hours before the end of his trip. This means that he had already traveled for a total of (t + u - 3) hours:

  t + u - 3 = (d / 70) + (d / 90) - 3

Simplifying this equation, we get:

  t + u = (9d / 630) + (7d / 630) + 3
  t + u = (16d / 630) + 3

We also know that Kevin's total travel time was (t + u) + 3 hours. Substituting the expression we just found for (t + u) into this equation, we get:

  (16d / 630) + 6 = (2d / 70) + (2d / 90)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

  d = 270

Response 9:
Knowledge:
  - Speed = Distance / Time
  - We can use the formula: Distance = Speed * Time to calculate the distance.
  - If d is the distance between A and B, then Kevin traveled a total of 2d miles (going from A to B and back).
  - Let t be the time it took Kevin to travel from A to B. Then, the time it took him to travel from B to A is also t (since he traveled at the same speed).
  - We know that he was 70 miles away from B when he had 3 hours left to complete the journey. This means that he had already traveled for t - 3 hours on his way back to A.
  - We can use the formula: Time = Distance / Speed to calculate the time it took him to travel from A to B and from B to 70 miles away from B.
  
Solution:
  - Let d be the distance between A and B.
  - The total distance Kevin traveled is 2d miles.
  - Let t be the time it took Kevin to travel from A to B.
  - The time it took him to travel from B to A is also t.
  - Let x be the time it took Kevin to travel from A to 70 miles away from B on his way back to A.
  - Then, the time it took him to travel from 70 miles away from B to B is t - x.
  - We know that he drove at a speed of 70 mph on his way from A to B, and 90 mph on his way back from B to A.
  - Therefore, we have:
    t = d / 70 (time taken to travel from A to B)
    t - x = (d - 70) / 90 (time taken to travel from 70 miles away from B to B)
  - We also know that he had 3 hours left to complete his journey when he was 70 miles away from B. This means that:
    t + (t - x) + 3 = (2d / 70) (total time taken for the whole journey)
  - Simplifying the above equation, we get:
    2t - x + 3 = (2d / 70)
  - Substituting t = d / 70 and t - x = (d - 70) / 90, we get:
    2(d / 70) - (d - 70) / 90 + 3 = 2d / 70
  - Simplifying the above equation, we get:
    d = 270
  - Therefore, the distance between A and B is 270 miles.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Let the number of employees be x, and the contribution of each employee be y. 

From the given information, we can form two equations:
1. xy = 600000
2. (x*y + 60x) = 624000

Simplifying the second equation, we get:
yx + 60x = 624000
x(y+60) = 624000
y+60 = 624000/x

Substituting this value of y+60 in the first equation, we get:
x*(624000/x - 60) = 600000
624000 - 60x = 600000
x = 400

Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Let's assume that there are 'n' employees in the organization, and each employee contributes 'x' amount of money. Therefore, the total amount collected would be n*x.

n*x = 6,00,000   ----- Equation 1
(n*x + n*60) = 6,24,000   ----- Equation 2
We need to find the value of 'n'.
Let's simplify Equation 2 by substituting Equation 1 in it:
6,00,000 + n*60 + n*x = 6,24,000
n*60 + n*x = 24,000
n*(60 + x) = 24,000
n = 24,000/(60 + x)
We need to find the value of 'n' which will be a whole number.
Let's try the given options one by one to check which value of 'n' gives us a whole number:
A: 300 employees, then x = 6,00,000/300 = 2000
Substituting the values in Equation 2: 300*60 + 300*2000 = 6,24,000, which is true.
So, the answer is 300.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 98 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A man divides Rs 8600 among 5 sons, 4 daughters and 2 nephews. If each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, and each son receives five as much as each nephew. How much does each daughter receive ?
Choices:
  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800
Response 0:
Let X be the amount each nephew receives. Therefore, each daughter will receive 4*X and each son will receive 5*X.

The total number of recipients is 5+4+2=11.

We can set up the following equation to solve for X:

5*5X + 4*4X + 2X = 8600
25X + 16X + 2X = 8600
43X = 8600
X = 200

So each nephew receives Rs 200, each daughter receives 4*X = Rs 800.

Action: Answer("E")

5(5x) + 4(4x) + 2(x) = 8600 

Simplifying the equation: 

25x + 16x + 2x = 8600 

43x = 8600 

x = 200 

So, each daughter receives 4 times as much as each nephew, which is 4 * 200 = Rs 800.

Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 2520
  C: 1728
  D: 1656
  E: None
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  To solve the problem, we need to use the formula: (7/8)x - (7/18)x = 770, where x is the unknown number.
  We can simplify the formula by finding the least common multiple of the denominators of 7/8 and 7/18, which is 72.
  Then, we can rewrite 7/8 and 7/18 with a denominator of 72: 7/8 = 63/72 and 7/18 = 28/72.
  So the formula becomes: (63/72)x - (28/72)x = 770.
  We can simplify further by combining the terms: (35/72)x = 770.
  To solve for x, we can multiply both sides by (72/35): x = (72/35) * 770 = 1584.

Question: Calculate the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 on a cab which charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
Choices:
  A: 11.75 miles
  B: 12.75 miles
  C: 17.75 miles
  D: 14.75 miles
  E: 10.75 miles
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
  We need to find the maximum distance that can be traveled with $8.50.
  To solve this problem, we need to use algebra.
  Let x be the number of quarter-miles traveled beyond the first quarter-mile.
  Then the total cost of the trip is 3.5 + 0.1x dollars.
  We want to find the maximum value of x such that 3.5 + 0.1x <= 8.5.
  Solving for x, we get x <= 50.
  Therefore, the maximum distance that can be traveled is (1 + 50/4) miles, which is 14.75 miles.

  We can solve the formula for distance in quarter-miles and then convert it to miles by dividing by 4.

  $5.00 - $3.50 = $1.50
  $1.50 ÷ $0.10 = 15 quarter-miles
  Now, we need to find how many quarter-miles we can travel with the remaining $3.50, which is:
  $3.50 ÷ $0.10 = 35 quarter-miles
  Therefore, the maximum distance we can travel is:
  (15 + 35) ÷ 4 = 12.5 miles
